Prime Minister van Zeeland is currently discussing this suggestion with the French government and has not yet submitted a reply. According to diplomatic figures, after receiving the Belgian notification, the French government warned the British government that the British proposal may be misinterpreted by Berlin as an acknowledgment by the signatory countries of the Locarno Pact of Germany's occupation of the Rhineland. The French government believes that Germany must first sincerely promise to respect the international rule of law before it can be acknowledged. (Agence Havas, 11th)

Therefore, it is preparing to participate in restoring the balance of power in Europe. The Rome correspondent of Le Petit Parisien reported today that Prime Minister Mussolini has expressed his willingness to send representatives to attend the Locarno Conference held in Brussels. (National Telegram, 10th)

(London) Official sources here announced today that although France has declared to Britain that the Anglo-French mutual assistance agreement in the Mediterranean will be abolished on July 15 when the League of Nations lifts sanctions against Italy, the mutual assistance agreements concluded with Britain by other countries such as Turkey, Yugoslavia, and Greece will remain in effect. (National Telegram, 10th)

(Paris) A correspondent from Le Petit Parisien reported from Rome that the Italian authorities were very satisfied after the French government announced that the mutual assistance measures previously agreed upon by Britain and France due to the situation in the Mediterranean would be invalidated. However, diplomatic figures believe that Italy may have accepted certain constraints on Germany and therefore cannot change its diplomatic policy. The current situation is still chaotic and subtle. American Heat Wave Not Retreating: Over 300 Deaths from Heatstroke 47

Forests Catch Fire Due to Heat, Thousands of Livestock Die, Britain Experiences Consecutive Days of Cool, Rainy Weather with Hailstones an Inch in Diameter

(New York) Except for northern New England, the rest of the United States is still suffering from the sweltering heat. As of today, the death toll has reached 375, thousands of acres of crops have withered due to drought, multiple forests have caught fire, and thousands of livestock have died. The Midwestern states have been particularly hard hit. The temperature in New York City reached 97 degrees Fahrenheit this afternoon. The mayor has ordered all employees except firefighters to stop working this afternoon to avoid heatstroke. 100,000 public relief workers have been sent back to their hometowns because many have collapsed from heatstroke. New York State is facing a water shortage, and the Department of Health has ordered people to conserve water. Light rain is forecast for the northwestern states on Sunday, but there is no sign of rain elsewhere. (Reuters, 10th)

Shippen Valley: As of today, at least 324 people have died from heatstroke. The drought in half of the United States has not improved. The losses to agricultural products and other properties are estimated to be around $250 million. If it does not rain, the losses will increase by $1 million per hour. Today, the temperature in two-thirds of the United States is above 100 degrees Fahrenheit. Although there are occasional thunderstorms in some areas, they do not help most of the disaster areas. In the 11 states most affected by the disaster, 5 million farmers have fallen into abject poverty in the past five weeks. (National Telegram, 10th)

(New York) The entire United States is currently being hit by a heat wave. As of now, there have been 303 deaths due to this. Ten people died from heatstroke this morning alone in this city. In some parts of the West, the temperature is as high as 49 degrees Celsius, which is 120 degrees Fahrenheit. The temperature in this city is 37.5 degrees Celsius, which is 99.4 degrees Fahrenheit. Mayor La Guardia has ordered all public officials in municipal government agencies, except for the police and fire departments, to stop working and return home to rest. 77 female employees in federal government agencies have fainted due to the extreme heat. All employees have also been ordered to stop working. (Agence Havas, 10th)

(New York) The entire United States has been hit by a heat wave for a month. There have been 375 deaths from heatstroke. In addition, the drought has caused severe damage to agricultural harvests. According to the estimates published by the Department of Agriculture on the 1st of this month, the losses are as follows: 805,420,000 bushels of buckwheat, 164,866,000 bushels of barley, and 1,237,764,000 pounds of tobacco. In addition, livestock have also been slaughtered due to water shortages. Currently, there are only 68,000,000 heads of livestock in the country. (Agence Havas, 10th)

(Washington) President Roosevelt told reporters today that he has started projects in the drought-stricken areas to employ 75,000 disaster victims, with 16,500 already working. He also said that there are 570,000 farmers affected by the drought. (Reuters, 10th)

(London) Britain is the opposite of the United States. The weather has been cool and rainy for consecutive days, causing great inconvenience to vacationers. All ball games have been stopped. There was a strong wind and rain in Eastbourne yesterday morning, with thunder rumbling like artillery fire, preceded by hailstones as large as stone bullets, accumulating to a depth of two inches. Hundreds of households were flooded and asked the fire department to pump out the water. Dozens of stores on Main Street were flooded, and goods flowed out of broken windows. As a cruise ship was approaching the dock, its mast touched an electric wire and broke. Captain Smith and a wireless telegraph operator were knocked down and suffered burns to their heads and necks. However, most of the passengers were in their cabins at the time, so they were not injured and most did not know that the mast had touched an electric wire. Shortly after, London and other places experienced heavy rain and hail. (Reuters, 11th)

German Zeppelin Hindenburg Suspected of Spying on Britain 50

Churchill Strongly Criticizes

(London) When the German zeppelin Hindenburg flew back to Germany from the United States a few days ago, it temporarily changed its route, citing weather reasons, and flew over the major industrial areas of northern Britain. Churchill, a member of parliament from the extreme conservative party, gave a speech in Chingdon, addressing this matter and strongly criticizing it, stating, "If a British aircraft, in clear weather, changes its route under the pretext of bad weather and flies over the German Heligoland, the Kiel Canal, or the newly built fortifications along the Rhine, what would Germany do? Predictably, its attitude would not be just a weak protest, like the bleating of a lamb, as we have done." Churchill then exposed the situation of Britain's inadequate military equipment, saying, "Last year, Germany's military spending was over £800 million, and this year it is even more than that. As far as I can see, we still need to make more efforts to ensure that our country's military spending does not appear to be inferior." (Agence Havas, 10th)

French Minister of Defense Explains Nationalization of Arms Industry 51

Stating There are Three Motives

(Paris) Cabinet Coordinator and Minister of National Defense Daladier recently made a declaration to the Finance Committee of the Chamber of Deputies, explaining the motives behind the government's proposed nationalization of the arms industry. He stated that the main motives for the proposal are threefold: to strengthen national defense, to prepare for industrial mobilization, and to exert a spiritual influence on foreign countries, thereby demonstrating the French government's firm will to permanently oversee armaments. Daladier also stated that the government's proposed bill is for nationalization, not a state monopoly, and that the government intends to nationalize only certain specific industries. The initial cost of implementation is estimated to be around 1 billion francs. (Havas dispatch, 10th)

(Berlin) During a recent meeting of the French Chamber of Deputies, right-wing member Grillis questioned Minister of Aviation Cot regarding the Aviation Ministry's supply of new-style machine guns for aircraft to Soviet Russia. After Cot's response, military circles here have paid great attention to the matter. Observers also stated that political figures were surprised by Minister Cot's statement that "no military alliance treaty exists between France and Russia." The Ministry of Foreign Affairs, upon hearing Minister Cot's declaration, expressed considerable optimism, stating that once the sanctions against Italy are decided to be lifted, the French government will end the previously agreed-upon Mediterranean mutual aid measures, which is commendable. It was also stated that "the French government now understands Italy's mindset and cannot accuse it of lacking sincerity towards Germany," and so on. (Havas dispatch, 11th)

(Paris) Minister of the Interior Salengro made a declaration in the Senate a few days ago, stating that the occupation of factories by striking workers must be stopped in the future. This declaration has recently been put into practice. A labor dispute occurred at the "Louis Lebeaudt Textile Factory" in this city several weeks ago. After negotiations between the factory and the striking workers, the majority of the workers, numbering over 750 men and women, have expressed acceptance of the terms for returning to work. However, a small group of approximately 100 people are still occupying the factory and refusing to return to work. The factory has strictly requested the local authorities to comply with the Minister of the Interior's declaration and provide assistance in ordering the striking workers to leave the factory. (Ginwas dispatch, 11th)

Avignon, France A disturbance occurred here today. A group of merchants, farmers, and small business owners marched to the city hall, singing the Marseillaise along the way. Another group of striking workers sang the Internationale and attacked the merchants. Several people on both sides sustained minor injuries. Police arrived and arrested six people. Subsequently, several people sang the Internationale, smashed the glass windows of a grocery store, and broke into the store to loot it before fleeing. The situation throughout the city is currently tense. (Havas dispatch, 10th)

(Paris) After the conflict between striking workers and merchants in Avignon, the Communist Party issued a public statement expressing regret, stating that the victory of the left-wing People's Front was due to the unity of the middle class and the working class. The events in Avignon are causing these two classes to be divided, which is regrettable. The main purpose of the People's Front is to protect the interests of both the working class and the middle class. In terms of the interests of the working class, improper actions should not be taken against the middle class, as there is a need for unity between these two classes. Otherwise, the strength of the people will be weakened by division, and the enemy of the people will inevitably take advantage of the opportunity to carry out their schemes, which is not what we want to see. (Havas dispatch, 10th)

(Paris) The joint conference of left-wing parties recently passed a letter to the people entitled "Upholding the Republican System." Its content expresses confidence in the declaration made by Minister of the Interior Salengro in the Senate a few days ago and earnestly urges workers to be self-restrained and not force the government to take coercive action. It stated that "the determination of the left-wing parties to implement the People's Front program is unshakable. Although these parties have a unified relationship with the working class, it is also essential to maintain public order. If strikers occupy factories indefinitely, the result will inevitably be the destruction of public order. There are currently some people spreading messages, exaggerating the labor movement, and the people should not easily believe them. As for the working class, if they take drastic actions, they may lose the sympathy of public opinion, which should be avoided." (Havas dispatch, 10th)

Ministry of Finance Revises Provisional Regulations on Foreign Liquor Tax 57

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance issued an order revising the Provisional Regulations on Foreign Liquor Tax, totaling thirteen articles. Key points: 1. For foreign liquors produced and sold within the country, excluding imported foreign liquors, which are subject to foreign liquor tax levied by the customs within the import tariff, and domestically produced foreign liquors that have been approved for the dispatch of personnel to reside in factories to collect taxes, which shall be handled in accordance with the Provisional Regulations on Foreign Liquor Tax Collected at Factories, all other foreign liquors, regardless of whether they are manufactured by foreigners or Chinese, shall pay taxes at the prescribed rates in accordance with these regulations. The foreign liquor tax shall be collected by the provincial tax authorities under the Ministry of Finance. In provinces where the consolidated tax and tobacco and alcohol tax have not been merged, it shall be temporarily handled by the tobacco and alcohol tax collection authorities. 2. The foreign liquor tax rate is temporarily set at 30% of the value, collected according to the value. It will not be levied repeatedly when sold to various places. 3. Merchants producing and selling foreign liquor must pay taxes and affix certificates before they are allowed to sell. (Special dispatch, 11th)

Page 11

Spain in Turmoil 61

Spanish peasants are the victims of a semi-feudal landlord system. In Spain, countless vestiges of feudalism and feudal psychology remain. Agricultural technology is as antiquated as in the days of Tsarist Russia, and production standards are extremely low. Profits are rarely reinvested; landlords lack confidence in their own future. The trouble with Spain is in the lazy rich and the lazy poor. I once visited a landlord who also served as a senior official in the local landlord association. As he spoke to me in a cafe, his head was turned elsewhere, and for the first fifteen minutes of our discussion, I carefully guarded against him. He felt that his class was advancing. He said, "I firmly believe that there is no way to improve agriculture except through irrigation" (in other words, this has nothing to do with the landlord). "Before the spread of socialism, the farmers, though dissatisfied, lived happily. The farmers are born in the fields and are accustomed to hard work. Although he feels that the wages are insufficient, he does not know what life improvement is. Wages are indeed miserable, but there is no possibility of increasing them now. Since 1931 (since the establishment of the Republic), agriculture has become unprofitable due to the rise in wages and the fall in prices. We are suffering from overproduction" (many Spaniards are starving to death).

"According to the actual will of mankind," he said automatically, "the problem of Spain is very easy to solve." I asked him to be more specific, but he only mentioned a few more nouns. Another manager of the Countess of Adanero's estate, which owns 50,000 hectares of land, also expressed the same sentiment.

The Spanish landlord class, which controls the lives of 80 percent of the population, will never solve the land problem (but this is the main problem in Spain), because it cannot solve it. Because farmers have no purchasing power. Therefore, various industries cannot develop. Spain lacks everything, and the number of unemployed in the cities alone has reached 700,000. People have very little money, very little consumption power, and therefore the national economy can only decline.

How does Azaña cope with this situation? He admits that this is a serious problem that needs urgent relief. To date, he has done this: forcibly leasing land to "Yunteros." In the worst-hit province of Cáceres, Señor de la Fuente, representative of the Land Reform Commission, issued a statement on March 7 demanding that landlords lease land to "Yunteros," but no one responded or compromised. Then the farmers submitted an "ultimatum": "If you don't give us land, we will occupy it within 48 hours!" On March 12, the farming area established by the Yunteros on the large estate began. Since then, 24,702 Yunteros in Cáceres have leased 69,612 hectares of land. But these lands are not confiscated or bought, and the Yunteros only become half-harvest shareholders. In this arid farming area, 30 to 35 hectares of land are required to support a family, while the Yunteros now receive an average of three hectares per household. A few people used to own some land, but these people are few and far between, and the old and new lands are often separated. Some Yunteros have to ride mules for five hours a day to get to the place where they cultivate. In Badajoz, the Land Reform Commission tried its best to promote the second province. On the evening of March 25, the farmers simply occupied the land, cultivated it automatically, and asked the commission to recognize their actions as legal—which was achieved. Here, the "Yunteros" can now also lease land. 45,000 Yunteros in Badajoz were allowed 12,000 hectares, an average of less than three hectares per person. Land reform is being promoted more or less everywhere, and will continue. Azaña once said to me, "When 500,000 farmers get land, this problem can be solved." Azaña also said that he hoped to confiscate the land of large landlords without compensation under the laws that had stopped several years ago. He will also allow the restoration of collective ownership of village land, which had been collective pastures ten years ago.

No one dares to say whether the Spanish peasant will finally enjoy his inadequate land. Minister of Agriculture Ruiz-Funeg told me, "This is a difficult problem." That's right. But this must be solved one day, the later the time, the more difficult it will be. At present, the Yunteros are still poor half-harvesters. Azaña said in my visit that land reform will strengthen the power of the urban bourgeoisie, but he doesn't care about this, because the bourgeoisie is not anti-Republican. But who can benefit from land reform after all? Maybe when land reform is completed, farmers can get a little benefit. But it can only be said that they can get some nourishment. This does not mean that he can become an active consumer of urban goods, which is inevitable. Should land reform be seen as a way to prosper Spanish cities and revitalize new industries? To do this, Azaña's plan is too narrow.

A subordinate of Azaña told me that land reform can weaken the power of the Socialist Party. It may have suppressed revolutionary enthusiasm. In my 2,000 kilometer car journey, the twenty Yunteros made it clear that they were satisfied with the land reform: although they also felt that it was still hopeless and unsuitable for them. The misery of Spanish farmers is imaginable. Only this minimum of attention and assistance has made them very grateful.

Therefore, Azaña's land reform may save Azaña himself, but he is also a giant who cannot be satisfied with this alone. His land reform will not save Spain. Now the Spanish resistance movement is practicing a promise of a class to seize power, so that the achievements of this class in Spain are the same as what the bourgeoisie has done in other countries—and then develop to a higher stage, but land reform weakens the power of this protest movement by partially comforting the rural unrest. It is sad that this is the case. If the peasants are satisfied with the current land reform, the implementation of the solutions that Spain needs will inevitably weaken the impetus politically.

This raises an interesting point: Azaña's reforms also weaken the landlord class. They are deprived of effective control over their property (unless the original reactionary politics are restored). Suppose this situation continues. Suppose that after three or two years, the farmers feel more dissatisfied with Azaña's moderate policies. Assuming they make the final demand for the confiscation and collectivization of all property, does the Spanish bourgeoisie have the power to resist? Perhaps Spain can democratically decide an economic revolution without a civil war. I don't know.

At the same time, the trend of agricultural collectivization is growing. I visited two collective villages. There are many more—all organized spontaneously by the farmers. They do not know the Soviet collective farms (Kolkozi). Fu De and Montojo (Jorge Montojo), the separate responsible persons for land reform in Cáceres and Badajoz, both felt that their institutions were inappropriate. They both saw the wisdom of broadcasting collectivization throughout Spain, especially in dry farming. Spanish law restricts the use of machinery in agriculture. The large-scale use of machinery for dry farming will inevitably give the Spanish countryside a new look. The landlords are unwilling to use it. Farmers are unable to do it personally. Collectivization is the most logical method. "But Spanish farmers are individualists," Ruiz-Funeg argued. I have heard this statement from many sources. I do not believe that extreme poverty is compatible with individualism. The individualist who has endured decades of poverty will inevitably agree to a collective system that can make him rich.

Lurgo Caba lero, the most popular leader of the left-wing Socialist Party—most of the farmers are left-wing socialists—told me that he did not believe that Azaña could implement collectivization. The Communist Party also holds the same view. They are afraid that the political situation may turn to the right again due to the conservative Lerroux and the reactionary Robles' attacks on Azaña's left-wing Republican Party. Will Azaña be destroyed by his party members? If so, then if the masses oppose his policies again, the crisis of giving the reactionaries a chance to rise may occur. Or the masses will support the Communist Party and Caballero (he told me that there is not much difference between him and the Communist Party) to continue Azaña's failed cause, but unless the right-wing comes up with a coup, this situation cannot happen immediately. The so-called "immediately" means at least a year.

Guangdong Province Plans to Issue Two Types of Public Bonds 75

Air Defense Bonds Rescheduled for October, Water Conservancy Bonds for Seven Million to be Issued in September

Guangzhou Correspondence: The Guangdong Provincial Government recently decided to issue two types of public bonds and has stepped up preparations. One is air defense bonds, which have a mandatory sales aspect. All men and women in cities, counties, and villages over the age of twenty must subscribe to bonds worth two jiao per person, collected in two installments, meaning each person must bear four jiao. Each county and city will establish a bond collection committee to be responsible for collecting the funds. The first installment was originally scheduled to begin on June 1, but due to insufficient preparation, it is proposed to reschedule it for October 1. The other is that the Guangdong government, in order to develop water conservancy and promote agriculture in the province, planned to issue water conservancy bonds last year to build water conservancy projects in various jurisdictions and repair various weirs. Later, it was decided to first issue seven million water conservancy bonds to repair the base weirs in the Pearl River Delta region. These bonds are to be divided into four denominations: ten yuan, fifty yuan, one hundred yuan, and one thousand yuan. Bonds with a face value of one thousand yuan account for one million yuan, bonds with a face value of one hundred yuan account for two million yuan, bonds with a face value of fifty yuan account for two million yuan, and bonds with a face value of ten yuan account for two million yuan. It is expected to be printed by the end of next month and will begin to be issued in September in order to collect funds and start construction in the autumn. The regulations for the issuance of Class A water conservancy bonds were revised by the provincial government yesterday as follows: Article 1: The Guangdong Provincial Government, in order to develop water conservancy in this province, specially allows the industrial and tenant groups in various jurisdictions to issue Class A rural construction bonds of Guangdong Province in the 25th year of the Republic of China. Article 2: The total amount of this bond is set at seven million silver legal currency of Guangdong Province, of which five million yuan will be used for the construction of base weirs in the Pearl River Delta region, and two million yuan will be used for the construction of water conservancy projects outside the Pearl River Delta region in this province, and shall not be used for other purposes. Article 3: The face value of this bond is set at four types: one thousand yuan, one hundred yuan, fifty yuan, and ten yuan. Article 4: The interest rate of this bond is set at one cent and two li per week, and interest will be paid once each at the end of January and July each year. Article 5: This bond is issued by the local water conservancy cooperative, and the government is responsible for paying interest and principal, and the government subsidizes one-sixth of the interest. Interest will only be paid during the period from the date of issuance to the date of completion of the project. One year after the date of benefit from the second construction after the completion of the project, the principal will be repaid, and it will be cleared by lottery ten times. One-tenth of the total amount will be drawn each time. The amount of interest and principal to be paid each time, whether the project is not completed or after it is completed, shall be drawn by the cooperative from the benefiting fields in advance by six months and deposited in the Guangdong Provincial Bank to prepare for the payment of interest and principal when due. Article 6: The payment of interest and principal of this provincial bond is guaranteed by the income from the fields. For example, after a base weir is to be built in a certain place, the local industry and tenants will set up a water conservancy cooperative in a certain place and submit a request to the government to issue bonds. The income from the fields in the weir will be used as a guarantee. The cooperative will be responsible for receiving the bonds, raising funds, building the base weir, and collecting the funds to be apportioned from the fields in the weir, and will be responsible for repaying the principal and interest of the bonds. Article 7: If this provincial bond cannot be repaid on time due to natural disasters or other irresistible failures, the government will designate the treasury tax revenue as the second guarantee and be responsible for the repayment. However, the government will still order the cooperative to recover the repaid funds from the income of the fields in installments until the debt is cleared. When necessary, the cooperative may apply to auction or lease the fields with outstanding debts to offset the repaid funds. Article 8: This bond is issued by the person in charge of the water conservancy cooperative that receives and issues the bond and is guaranteed by the Director of the Guangdong Department of Finance. Article 9: The matters concerning the payment of interest and principal of this bond may be handled by the cooperative that issues the bond after submitting an application to the Department of Finance for approval and entrusting it to the Guangdong Provincial Bank. Article 10: This bond is an un-registered type and can be freely bought and sold and can be used as a reserve for bank guarantees and other public guarantees and collateral. Article 11: Any act of forging this bond and damaging its credit shall be punished according to law. Article 12: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation. (July 6)

Page 12

North China Smuggled Goods Shift to Jiangsu and Anhui 76

Japanese Crackdown on Ronin is an Illusion, Smuggling Adopts Water and Land Liaison Method, Aiming to Open Up New Sales Markets in the South

Tianjin Correspondence: The Japanese military headquarters in Tianjin and the Japanese Consulate General in Tianjin have recently cracked down on smuggling and Japanese and Korean ronin participating in various organizations. Among them, the Japanese military department is particularly concerned about smuggling ronin groups such as trade associations. They have warned them not to obstruct traffic. If they have to use the railway, they must pay according to regulations. The Japanese Consulate General summoned the chairman of the Korean Association to instruct him to tell the Koreans that those engaged in special trade (i.e., smuggling) must seek safe transportation methods. If they rely on group organizations to force transportation agencies to carry goods, it is easy to cause Chinese-Japanese animosity. It will absolutely not be allowed in the future. The consulate also ordered the police chief, Kazukui, to be responsible for the investigation and prohibition. This move by the Japanese seems to be quite satisfactory in the midst of rampant smuggling in North China. However, according to the investigation, the Japanese military department and the Japanese Consulate General are only feigning, showing us verbal benefits, because the clarification of the North China political power that the Japanese have been expecting recently is being urged from all sides, forcing its realization. However, because rampant smuggling affects North China's tax revenue, they are worried that this will hinder the implementation of North China's new plans, so they have repeatedly declared that they will crack down on illegal ronin and smuggling groups. In the past week, they have expelled eighteen Koreans and seven Japanese to their home countries to show their determination. In fact, those who were expelled just exited through Tanggu and then returned from Yu Guan. It's just a trick. The smuggling situation at Tianjin East Station is still the same as before.

In the past half month, the goods smuggled southward from Tianjin have not been as many as before. On average, about 180 to 200 pieces of artificial silk and about 80 to 130 companions of sugar are transported southward on the Tianjin-Pukou Train No. 305 every night. In addition, there are needles, printed matter, cigarette paper, and beer. The reason for the decrease is that too many smuggled goods are stored in Tianjin, and the prices have fallen, and there is no market. At the same time, smuggled goods are also flooding Jinan, and sales are too slow. The goods are transported there and piled up like in Tianjin. South of Xuzhou, the inspection is strict, and low-taxed Japanese goods cannot be transported there. Because goods are piled up in Tianjin, it indirectly affects the promotion of smuggled goods in Dalian and eastern Hebei. It is said that Dalian currently has 50,000 bags of sugar, which are expected to be transported and sold after half a year. About 2 million pieces of artificial silk are stored in the coastal areas of Qinhuangdao, Nandaisi, and Beidaihe in eastern Hebei. Although each storage place has iron-tiled warehouses, the rainy season is coming. If there is rainy weather, the iron-tiled warehouses cannot cover them. The goods do not have to be damaged by rain leaks, and the evaporation of ground moisture is enough to cause mildew and rot. Therefore, the smuggling ronin are working hard to find safe methods and plan to abandon the warehouses in Qinhuangdao, Nandaisi, and Beidaihe and use the stacking yards in Luangekou and Liushouying exclusively. They will add solid moisture-proof works and move all the goods to the area for storage. In the future, the smuggling route, since the customs patrol ship Yu Guang was monitored by the Japanese warships, the Qikou Zhao Jiagou area on the sea has been unimpeded, so it is planned to use water and land liaison. The goods are loaded on steamships from Dalian and transported to Qikou, and then transported by horse-drawn carts and mules to the hinterland of Hebei, Shandong, Henan, and Jiangsu provinces to avoid the inspection offices in Xuzhou and gradually sell them along the Yangtze River. The ronin now feel that there is no better plan than to open up sales channels in Jiangsu and Anhui. If this road is blocked, the North China market will remain stagnant, and the future of smuggling will completely fall into pessimism.

A lot of cotton yarn is also transported in the smuggled goods. Gaoyang in southern Hebei and Zhoucun in western Shandong are both local cloth producing areas and used to purchase finished products from the Tianjin-Jinan yarn factories. Since smuggled cotton has been selling well, the sales of Tianjin-Jinan national yarn have gradually declined. The Hengyuan, Beiyang, and Huaxin yarn factories in Tianjin have to lose 1,500 to 2,500 yuan per day. A month ago, each bag of yarn was sold at a loss of only 10 yuan due to the dumping of Japanese yarn, but now it is more than that. Sometimes it has to lose 20 to 30 yuan. The yarn market transaction is not enough to control the private sales of yarn. In order to save themselves, the factories recently agreed to adopt a joint operation and mutual support method to work hard to resist Japanese yarn. If the struggle is effective, the future is still promising. Otherwise, before the Japanese yarn monopoly plan in China succeeds, we will be exhausted and unable to support it. (10th)

Wang Kemin Arrives in Beiping on a Mission 77

He Had Discussions with Relevant Parties When Passing Through Tianjin; Meeting With Important Chinese and Japanese Figures in Beiping and Will Soon Return South

Beiping Correspondence: Wang Kemin, a member of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee, recently went north from Shanghai at the invitation of Song Zheyuan, the chairman of the committee. After paying a visit to President Jiang in Nanjing to ask for instructions on everything, he took the Shanghai-Beiping train and went directly to Tianjin. After Wang got off the train and exchanged greetings with Qin and others, he went to the Beijing Hotel to stay. Japanese Soldiers Show Off Their Power in Beiping 78

Tank Car Trial Runs on the 8th and 9th, Field Exercise in Western Beiping on the 10th

Citizens Alarmed, Roads Destroyed 79

Beiping Correspondence: After the increase of the Japanese garrison in North China, the garrison locations have been completely allocated. The Japanese troops in various places have been allocated trucks and tank cars by the Japanese military headquarters. After the Japanese troops stationed in Fengtai received the tank cars, they notified us to hold a test run exercise on the 8th and 9th. On the morning of the 10th, they also held a field exercise at Lugouqiao in western Beiping. On the 8th, the first day, more than 100 Japanese soldiers from Fengtai, led by more than 10 officers, took trucks and brought nine tank cars, four large and five small (all weighing less than five tons), and drove from Fengtai to Nanyuan. After a short rest, they went straight into Yongdingmen, passed through Tianqiao Qianmen Street, Dongxi Jiaomin Lane, exited Hepingmen, went south along Xizhushikou to Tiantan for a rest. At about 5:00 p.m., they left Tiantan and went west, exited Guang'anmen and returned to Fengtai. On the 9th, the second day, at about 9:00 a.m., more than 100 Japanese soldiers again took eight trucks, two motorcycles, and seven large and small tank cars, and entered Guang'anmen from Fengtai via Nanyuan. They drove east for about three li and turned north into Qianmen. It was already noon. A part of them stopped in front of Tiananmen for a rest, and a part of them rested in Xipishi inside Qianmen. There were armed Japanese soldiers with guns guarding the tank cars. After a short rest, the soldiers had lunch in the trucks, and the officers had a picnic at the back door of Zhongshan Park. At 2:30, they gathered again and exited Qianmen, entered Chongwenmen via Dongzhushikou, and went north. At 4:30, they went to Chaoyangmen for an exercise. They rested at Miaojiadi Target Pavilion that night. At 10:00 a.m. on the 10th, they went to Lugouqiao in western Beiping again for a field exercise. After completion, they returned to the Fengtai barracks. When armed Japanese soldiers entered the city to parade on the 8th and 9th, many pedestrians stopped to watch and discussed this kind of demonstration. At noon on the 9th, when the Japanese soldiers were resting in Xipishi, an American man came in a car with the number 499 to take pictures. After being discovered by the Japanese soldiers, they firmly refused. The American man had no choice but to be persuaded to leave. After this decisive Japanese soldier entered the city to parade, the asphalt roads in the city were mostly loose and melted due to the hot weather in recent days. In addition, they were crushed by a large number of trucks and heavy tank cars, resulting in damage in many places. More than 80 Japanese soldiers stationed in Beiping, fully armed with rifles and machine guns, left the barracks in a team at 8:00 a.m. on the 9th and went to the Wangye Tomb and Dongdaqiao area in the eastern suburbs for an exercise without lead arrows. They finished at about 2:00 p.m. and returned to Beiping along the Beining Railway Beiping Tongxian Railway branch line. They also practiced street fighting along the way. The nearby residents did not know what was going on and were all alarmed. At about 5:00 p.m., the Japanese soldiers entered the city. (9th)

Financial and Commercial Situation in Jiangxi Province at the End of the Year 80

Economic Recession Affects People's Livelihood, Stores Go Bankrupt and Crave Relief, Yuan Ticket Problem is Also Very Important

Nanchang Correspondence: The banks in this city closed for three days from the 1st to the 3rd to make the settlement for the 24th year. The Central Bank, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Shanghai Bank, Continental Bank, National Products Bank, Construction Bank, and Farmers Bank (the above are branches in Shanghai), Yumin, and Municipal Second Vocational (local banks) all have surpluses, ranging from tens of thousands of yuan to a few thousand yuan. However, due to the sluggish market, they all adopted a tight policy in the year, and did not make credit loans, but only did door-to-door remittances and commodity mortgages, with a very small scope, and the profit was only one-third of the previous year. In the 25th year, except for the Farmers Bank and the Bank of China, which will carry out rural loans, the rest are in a state of shrinking stagnation and cannot break the deadlock, while a group of shops and rural areas have no capital to turn around, losing the exchange function, with difficulties both above and below, and the social finance and people's livelihood are in extreme distress and uneasiness.

In the 24th year, Nanchang's commerce, due to the aftermath of the banditry of the previous year, coupled with the bankruptcy of the rural economy, the amount of import and export trade decreased by 10 million yuan in one year. Large and small shops all felt that income was not enough to cover expenses and it was difficult to maintain. As of the end of the lunar year last year, 300 shops have reported bankruptcy. Since the beginning of this year, the situation has deteriorated. According to the Public Security Bureau's investigation, the number of shops closing down every month is between 40 and 50, which means that nearly 300 shops will have closed down in the first half of this year. The most prosperous Zhongshan Road, such as Wanlong, Huyuanxing, Zhang Zhengshun, Wu Anxiang, etc., are all locked up. Zhongzheng Road, such as Hong Kong Silver Building, Lianfu, Zhou Senxing, Fengfu, Tianfu, Jingchang, etc., have no way to open. Even those who barely open their doors are enduring the pain. The money industry, which was previously relied upon by all industries for turnover, is also unable to protect itself and will not last long, because money shops have limited funds and rely entirely on absorbing social deposits, floating funds, and store discounts to turn around. Therefore, what all industries are relying on for relief now is only the credit and mortgage loans of the banks. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce is requesting the Provincial Yumin Bank to provide mortgage loans to relieve all industries. The method is that the shops borrowing the loans first report the collateral to the industry association, and then apply to the bank for approval. In addition to the collateral, two shop guarantees are required. The amount is from 300 yuan to 3,000 yuan per household. The interest rate and term are the same as the year-end loans of the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications last year. Yuhang is still waiting and seeing this, but people in the financial world say that Yuhang has an original share capital of 2 million yuan and the right to issue more than 1 million yuan of auxiliary coins and copper yuan tickets. Now, because the market is sluggish and the collapse is very strong, there is no business to do, and in the future, it must make mortgage loans. Although the mortgage is a stagnant fund, the bank has the right to issue it, which can be used for turnover, and the market has collapsed to this point. If the public bank does not provide relief, it will be destroyed together.

There is also a financial problem in this province, which is the copper yuan ticket. Originally, there were three banks issuing copper yuan tickets in this city: Yumin, Municipal, and Construction. The number of yuan tickets circulating in the market is about one million strings (1,000 characters per unit). When the monetary system was reformed earlier, it was stipulated that each legal tender would be exchanged for 3,500 characters of yuan tickets. Since the price in various places was 3,000 characters, the money industry hoarded a large amount of yuan tickets and requested that it be changed to 3,000 for sea yuan. The three banks had to recover the yuan tickets that had been circulated before changing it to 3,000. There was a dispute, so a group of people refused to circulate the yuan tickets, making it extremely difficult to find change. Some used a few copper coins with a stamped note to find change, and some tore the yuan tickets into several pieces to find change. The most suffering are the coolies and hawkers, and the beggars also could not get a single penny all day long because there were no copper coins. The price of copper yuan tickets, which is closely related to the lower class, urgently needs to be changed to 3,000, so that it can be used consistently for turnover. (July 7)

Taicang Laogongmao Announces Liquidation 81

In this county's sauce and wine industry, there were originally two companies, Wanquanyu and Laogongmao, with substantial capital and a wide range of businesses, with branches spread all over the county. After Wanquanyu went bankrupt the year before last, the only one left was Laogongmao, which had also experienced twists and turns. It was later maintained by shareholder Chen Shiqin. Three years later, due to sluggish finances and poor turnover, it closed down on the 9th, including all its branches, and entrusted lawyer Wang Kunfu to announce the liquidation. It is heard that the amount of deposit and loan has reached more than 300,000 yuan, and Chen is willing to use the field property to compensate for the debt.

Kunshan Changshu Tangwei Bank Completed 82

The Tangwei Bank in Changshu County is of great importance to farmland water conservancy. However, due to years of disrepair, it was dilapidated. The county government instructed the First District Office to repair it in April. After planning and decision, the method of labor relief was adopted. Since the start of construction, it has been three months, and the entire project has been completed, with a total of more than 30,000 cubic meters of earthwork. The cost is relatively reduced due to labor relief, with a total cost of more than 3,000 yuan. It will be submitted to the county for inspection and acceptance soon.

There are many Jiangbei fishermen in each district of this county, who engage in Zhang Lan digging eels in the summer. However, the newly planted green seedlings in the farmland are damaged. If there is a flood one day, the weirs will be in danger of collapsing. The county government, in view of this, specially ordered the Public Security Bureau on the 10th to strictly prohibit it in order to benefit the farmland.

Zhou She Massacre Sentenced 84

In a household in Jia Quan'gui, a farmer in Zhaozhuangjia Village, Wanxiang Township, Zhou She, the eighth district of Yishu, and his wife Wu were brutally murdered by their lover and others on the night of May 11. After the authorities investigated and clarified the matter, Wu Juchang, Wu's brother, Yu Jingen, Lu Jingen, the lover, and the persons involved in the case were all arrested. After several interrogations by the judiciary, the sentence was pronounced on the 10th. Wu Juchang and Yu Jingen were sentenced to death for jointly murdering. Lu Jingen was sentenced to life imprisonment, and the rest were acquitted.

Xu Liangqiu and other seven trainees of the central primary school in this county who went to the town for training have returned to Kunshan on the 10th after completing their training. Suzhou Jiang Yaoji Owes Taxes and Is Escorted to the County 86

Jiang Yaoji, the former director of the tooth tax collection in this county, lost more than 7,000 yuan of public funds due to operating other businesses. The county escorted Jiang to the county for pursuit. Later, Hang Zishan bailed Jiang out, willing to compensate for the 7,000 yuan of public funds, so Jiang was able to regain his freedom. Qian Qianji, the current tooth tax collector of Wuxian County, is a young child only ten years old, and his person in charge is still Jiang Yaoji.

Wanted Smuggler Xu Ziyun 87

The smuggler Xu Ziyun was arrested last month, and was deceived by his Yiting and tried to bail him out. Later, Wu Ada was entrusted to take his place and surrendered to the authorities to await punishment. Deng Xianchang learned of this and presented it to the Fanbei Command for approval. Wu Ada was sent to the local court for strict handling, and on the 11th, he presented it to the Minting to order all counties to jointly arrest Xu Ziyun and bring him to justice for investigation.

Changshu Hupu Fish Market Falls Miserably 88

Hupu Town along the river in this county is a famous fish market in Jiangsu Province. Every spring and summer, the ocean floods are very prosperous, and most merchants from all over the world go to Hupu to set up temporary shops, and their lives are quite developed, commonly known as rushing to the ocean flood. It is now midsummer, and the fish flood has ended. According to the fish merchants in the town, this year's fish flood is very different from last year's business. According to statistics, the income is less than 60% of that of previous years, and the expenses are huge. Most of the fish businesses have losses and no profits, and other temporary shops that rushed to the ocean flood also have bleak lives and are greatly affected. Now that the fish market is about to end, the merchants have no way to end it. Zhou Yinhuai, the owner of a fish business, and others have initiated and collected funds to perform dramas to revitalize the market and save this declining market.

Patrol Officer Accused of Adultery with Clerk's Wife 89

Wang Shou-xuan, the current patrol officer of the Meili Third Sub-bureau, is accused of having an affair with Xu Mei-jun, the wife of a clerk named Cao. Cao has allegedly gone insane and attempted suicide multiple times. The General Bureau is currently thoroughly investigating the matter. It is reported that Wang Shou-xuan was originally a patrol officer at the Sixth Precinct. Cao, a clerk under his command, was his fellow townsman. Cao's wife, Xu Mei-jun, married him the year before last. Because there was no one to care for them in their hometown, he brought her to Changzhou, where they lived together. Recently, the bureau ordered Cao to be transferred to the Seventh Precinct and his wife was temporarily lodged at Patrol Officer Wang's place. Unexpectedly, Wang had an affair with Xu. When Cao sent a letter to take her back, Wang ignored it. When Cao went to pick her up in person, he learned the truth. She had already gone to the city with Patrol Officer Wang. Cao, in a moment of anger and unbearable grief, attempted to drown himself in the river multiple times. Fortunately, he was rescued each time. He is now in a state of insanity. The matter was reported to the General Bureau, which will conduct a thorough investigation.

Jiangyin to Dredge City River in Autumn 91

The provincial government has cut more than 50,000 yuan from the county's construction funds for the 25th year of the Republic. County Magistrate Yuan, noting that the dredging of the city river and the construction of Junjiang Road were urgently needed but there were no funds available, immediately sent Chief Chen Bingzhang of the Third Section to the province to explain the situation and request instructions. The provincial authorities considered the dredging of the city river to be urgent and approved an appropriation from the Jiangnan Water Conservancy Engineering Office to subsidize the project, with preparations underway to begin construction in the autumn. The construction of Junjiang Road will be postponed due to lack of funds.

Disposition of Smuggled Goods Seized in Yangzhou's Fourth District 92

Previously, the special task force of the Fourth District Division of the Waterborne Provincial Public Security Bureau intercepted a civilian smuggling vessel at the Jiangdu Guazhou River estuary. The vessel was carrying over two hundred bolts of plain white cloth without the required shipping documents. Interrogation revealed that the goods originated from the Yongfengyu Cloth Factory in Wuhu. Upon receiving this information, the Wuhu Public Security Bureau dispatched Inspector Rao, along with Manager Lu of the factory, to Guazhou to identify the cloth as the original stolen goods from the factory. The district department then handed over the boatman, Peng Desheng, along with the smuggled cloth, to the officers for return to the Wuhu Public Security Bureau for investigation. It was also learned that the Third Detachment of the district, stationed in Baoying, intercepted the Huo Qingban Datong steamer, towing three civilian smuggling vessels. The goods lacked shipping documents. Two civilian vessels from Zhenjiang Kaibao had goods that did not match the manifests. In addition to reporting to the district headquarters and classifying the goods without documents as smuggled goods awaiting disposition, customs inspectors were dispatched to investigate the two vessels of Zhang Heshang and Chen Changming, whose manifests were inconsistent. Customs Supervisor Ge Daxi and Examiner Wang Zongjun boarded the Zhenping steamer to investigate. It is reported that the goods included white and red sugar, dried scallops, dyes, etc. Those with valid customs declarations were immediately released, while others were detained, pending instructions from customs.

Revision of Land Tax Regulations 93

The Jiangdu County Government, in order to revise the land tax regulations for the 25th year of the Republic, convened a meeting of district chiefs at 3:00 PM on the 10th. Chairman Shen Youchen decided on three principles: 　The tax burden should be reduced in the east based on the reports from townships and towns in each district and the findings of committee members' on-site inspections. 　The reduction standard should be determined based on the fertility of the land and the usual income situation, with the total amount of tax reduction not exceeding 60,000 yuan. 　The grassy beaches will continue to be taxed according to the third-class lower rate of the 24th year, with each mu paying one jiao. A plan to combine two mu into one mu for tax purposes will be proposed to the provincial government for approval and implemented in the 26th year.

Luhe Strictly Prohibits Usurious Lending 94

In various townships and towns of this county, there are unscrupulous individuals who, before the wheat has been harvested in summer and after the autumn rice has just been transplanted, provide loans to villagers, stipulating repayment at harvest time, imposing heavy interest, and exhausting the people. The county government has previously issued a notice prohibiting this practice, but these individuals have become accustomed to disregarding the law and have reverted to their old ways, defying the prohibition. The general public, aware of this situation, recently sent representatives to the county government to file a petition, earnestly pleading for action. County Magistrate Qi believes that this matter is prohibited by law and that the petition is reasonable. He has reissued the prohibition order and instructed the district chiefs to strictly investigate and prohibit the practice.

Ningbo Uncovers Smuggling Organization 95

The Zhejiang Maritime Customs Superintendent's Office uncovered a smuggling organization last month in Xiashafang Bridge, Anchang, Shaoxing. They seized fourteen packages of rayon and arrested a well-known smuggler named Shen Baosheng. The suspects and evidence were handed over to the Yin County District Court Prosecutor's Office for investigation. After interrogation by Chief Prosecutor Gao, the defendant Shen Baosheng was detained. On the morning of the 8th, Sheng Xiangling, Wu Dezai, and Chen Yuanyu, who were involved in the case, were summoned to court for questioning. Sheng Xiangling (manager of the Shaoxing Fuyuan Silk and Satin Shop) was suspected of being involved in smuggling and was released on bail of 5,000 yuan. Shen Baosheng remains in custody pending trial.

Bandits Discovered in Mount Dalan 96

Large bands of bandits have recently been discovered near Mount Dalan, which borders the counties of Xin, Sheng, Yin, and Feng. The situation is reportedly very rampant. Upon receiving this report, the Yin County District Security Command immediately ordered the Third Company of the First Battalion of the Security Force stationed in Xiangshan, and the Fifth Battalion of the Security Force stationed in Ninghai to rush to suppress them.

Yuyao Urges Reporting of Stored Grain 97

In Yuyao, the implementation of grain storage has been accompanied by soaring prices. Some individuals have reportedly taken advantage of handling fees to sell the stored grain and embezzle the proceeds. Handling personnel have concealed their reports and failed to turn over the funds, intending to enrich themselves. After hearing about this, County Magistrate Lin issued a special order to the township chiefs yesterday, urging them to promptly report the amount of grain received and the details of expenditures, and to make the information public to dispel doubts.

Xiaoshan Decides on Opening of Zha Cao Road 98

The Ministry of Railways, together with the Zhejiang Provincial Government, is actively constructing the Qianjiang Bridge. Once completed, the railway lines on both sides of the Qianjiang River will be directly connected, and the entire Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway will be operational. To this end, the Ministry has borrowed a large sum from the Construction Bank of China and is actively planning to build the Zha Cao section from Zhakou through Xiaoshan and Shaoxing to Cao'e. A large bridge will also be built over the Cao'e River to connect with the Yong Cao section. In the future, passengers will be able to travel from Shanghai to Ningbo from morning to evening. The route from Zhakou over the Qianjiang Bridge to Cao'e has already been surveyed. It has been decided to borrow the Hangzhou Railway line from the edge of Nanjiang along Jingjiang Station to Xiaoshan and relay heavy-duty rails. The land acquisition for the roadbed from Xiaoshan to Cao'e is underway. In order to complete the connecting engineering of the Zha Cao section quickly, the Ministry of Railways has already decided to send Zhang Haiping to Zhejiang to preside over the connecting rail engineering of the section. The formal announcement will be made in the coming days. However, the date of commencement of construction is yet to be determined. It is reported that the Ministry of Railways believes that the Qianjiang Bridge will soon be completed, and that this connecting engineering should be completed as soon as possible. Therefore, it has been decided that the connecting of the rails must be completed within ten months from the date of commencement of construction to achieve direct traffic between Ningbo and Shanghai.

Taizhou Executes Town Chief for False Accusation 99

Zheng Songpo, the town chief of Canhuan Town in Wenling, had a long-standing grudge against a local named Shan Changbiao. In October of last year, he falsely accused Shan of manufacturing opium pills and communicating with bandits by placing twenty-six red pill bags, five taels of opium pills, and one bandit note in Shan's house and reporting it to the county government. The county government immediately dispatched police to the scene, led by Songpo, and arrested Changbiao. Shan claimed to be unjustly accused and requested a thorough investigation. The county government summoned Town Chief Zheng to the county for questioning. After investigation, detention, and multiple interrogations, the truth became clear. Songpo was sentenced to death according to law. The execution was reported to and approved by the Anti-Opium Commissioner of the Military Affairs Commission. At 9:00 AM on the 7th, Zheng Songpo was identified, bound, and taken to the execution ground outside the South Gate, where he was executed by firing squad.

Bengbu Uncovers Counterfeit Currency Ring 100

It has been reported that counterfeit currency has been frequently discovered in recent months. The Public Security Bureau has previously uncovered cases of manufacturing and using counterfeit currency and handed the suspects and evidence over to the court for punishment. However, these individuals continue to secretly counterfeit currency for profit. On the 8th, detectives from the Public Security Bureau discovered 586.10 yuan in counterfeit paper currency and multiple forged military documents at the home of Pan Jiabin in Panjia Village, south of Bengbu Mountain. The suspects Pan Jiabin, his wife Pan Li, his son Pan Shaoqing, and suspected accomplices Li Degong, Huang Peiru, and Yang Guilin were arrested and taken to the bureau for questioning. On the 9th, the bureau sent personnel to continue the investigation. Later, Sun Desheng and Zhang Zhongcheng were apprehended at the railway station. Sixty-three yuan in counterfeit coins, ten yuan in counterfeit paper money, and a military certificate were found on their persons. The principal offender, Zhou Jinde, is at large. Sun and Zhang, along with Pan Jiabin and others, have been transferred to the court for trial.

Chen Guangfu and Others Return to Shanghai Yesterday 101

Talks on negotiations in the United States to be delivered; will go to Beijing tonight to report to the authorities.

Chen Guangfu, General Manager of the Shanghai Commercial Bank, Guo Bingwen, Director of the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, and Gu Yiqun, Counselor of the Executive Yuan, who were sent to the United States to discuss monetary issues, left the country for the United States on March 13 of this year. They had discussions and negotiations with the U.S. Treasury Department officials. After the matter was completed, they went to Europe and returned to China on the German postal ship "Bostan". They arrived in Shanghai at around 5:00 PM yesterday. Figures in the financial world of Shanghai went to welcome them. Mr. Chen and others gave speeches on board and decided to go to Beijing tonight to report. Details are as follows.

Welcoming Personnel: Those who arrived to welcome them yesterday afternoon included Chen Xing, Ye Zhuotang, Xi Demao, Shou Yicheng, Song Hanzhang, Qian Xinzhi, Bei Songsun, Ye Fuxiao, Du Yuesheng, Tang Shoumin, Zou Bingwen, Yang Jiemei, Sun Ruihuang, Shi Boqun, Cheng Lian of the banking world, Zhang Yujiu, Ji Zejin of the International Trade Bureau, Gao Dazhong of the Ministry of Railways, Sun Silin, Tong Runfu of the National Economic Council Cotton Control Association, Huang Boqiao of the Two Roads Bureau, Chen Peide, Chen Juchuan, Jiang Huaisu of the Zhenjiang Shanghai Association, Rong Hongkang of Shenxin Textile Factory, and more than a hundred family members of the three gentlemen, all standing under the scorching sun, looking eastward. At 4 o'clock, the "Bostan" slowly entered the port and docked at about 5 o'clock. The welcoming personnel immediately went up the stairs to the ship. Mr. Chen and others met in the main restaurant. Mr. Guo Bingwen entertained them on behalf of Mr. Chen. After shaking hands with Mr. Chen and others, they returned to shore one after another.

Speeches Delivered: Mr. Chen and others met with reporters on board and delivered a written statement saying: "In March of this year, Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance commissioned us to go to the United States to discuss monetary issues related to China and the United States and to investigate the economic, financial, and trade conditions of various countries. After arriving in the United States, we were warmly received by the U.S. Treasury Department, and we discussed cooperation issues with us in a very sincere manner. After seven weeks of long discussions, the U.S. and Chinese Treasury Departments reached a practical cooperation method. The content has been seen in the declarations of Minister Kong and Mr. Morgen-thau. In general, we will maintain an independent and independent monetary system and try to promote the use of silver. The United States will purchase silver from China and provide us with the convenience of U.S. currency at any time. After this negotiation, our already substantial foreign exchange reserves will be significantly increased, sufficient to maintain the external value of our currency and make it impossible to shake. Therefore, our monetary reform has been truly successful, and the foundation for economic recovery has begun. On the other hand, the world price of silver can also be stabilized, realizing the long-standing proposition of China and the United States and laying the foundation for future economic cooperation between the two countries. This is what those who are involved in it feel extremely happy about. When this was decided in Washington, President Roosevelt kept asking about the progress of the talks and was very satisfied with the results of the talks. The U.S. authorities, including President Roosevelt and key members of the Ministry of Finance and external affairs, as well as congressional leaders such as Mr. Pittman, are deeply interested in the progress of monetary reform led by our Ministry of Finance and do not hesitate to provide assistance. All sectors of American society also expressed sympathy for our various efforts, which is admirable. As for the results of the talks, since the main purpose is to promote the stability of our currency, the conditions that we abide by should be implemented as soon as possible. The improvement of our central bank should also be realized as soon as possible, so that it can become the sole manager of our currency and credit and bring the national finance into the right track."

Going to Beijing Tonight: He continued, "When returning from the United States and Europe, we took the opportunity to investigate the latest trends in the world economy, finance, and trade. We will try to use what we have learned when serving the country to fulfill the duties of a citizen." In addition, reporters asked Mr. Chen and others whether they had gone to England to conclude an agreement on the sale of silver in London. According to reports, when passing through Hong Kong, reporters there also asked about this. In fact, Mr. Chen and others went to Europe from the United States in early June and returned to China by ship through France and Italy. They did not actually go to the United Kingdom, so there was no agreement with England. It is a rumor that does not need to be denied. "He then got off the ship and returned home to rest. It is heard that the Central Bank has reported to Finance Minister Kong in Beijing and decided to go to Beijing tonight to report the process to the authorities."

Draft Agreement on Factory Inspection: Consular Body Requests Amendment 102

Saying that it cannot be applied to factories in countries with consular jurisdiction. Since Municipal Secretary-General Yu Hongjun and Shanghai Municipal Council Director-General Fessenden discussed the draft "Agreement on the Implementation of the Factory Law in the Shanghai International Settlement," which was passed by the Municipal Council Board of Directors on the 24th of last month, the Japanese side opposed it. For the sake of caution, the Municipal Council applied to the Consular Body for ratification again on the next day (the 25th). Unexpectedly, the Consular Body's meeting the day before yesterday failed to pass the draft as it was and requested that it be amended.

Consular Body Resolution: The Consular Body did not hold a meeting until 2:30 PM the day before yesterday. The head consul, British Consul-General in Shanghai, Brenan, convened a meeting in the Municipal Council Board of Directors meeting room. U.S. Consul-General Gauss, Japanese Consul Terasaki, Italian Consul-General Nilon, Belgian Consul-General Tanerfu, Norwegian Acting Consul-General Kierde, Swedish Consul-General Beck-Friis, Swiss Consul-General Raudi, Dutch Consul-General Bousquet, Danish Consul-General Heer, Portuguese Consul-General Alves, Spanish Consul-General Fure, Brazilian Consul-General Branco, etc. all attended. The meeting was chaired by Mr. Brenan. After a long discussion, there was no objection to the principles of the agreement. However, if no distinction was made between countries with consular jurisdiction and countries without consular jurisdiction, and the agreement was followed across the board, it would not be acceptable and would have to be amended. That is, the agreement could only be applied to Chinese factories and factories in countries without consular jurisdiction within the Settlement. Factories in countries with consular jurisdiction could not be cited. It was resolved that the head consul would reply to the Municipal Council by letter to this effect. The meeting lasted for an hour before it was adjourned.

Reply to the Chairman of the Municipal Council: Head Consul and British Consul-General Brenan, based on the resolution of the Consular Body meeting, sent a letter to Arnold, Chairman of the Municipal Council, at 11:00 AM yesterday to reply. The original letter is translated as follows: "In reply, I have received your letter of June 25 from the Director-General. I am now authorized to reply that the Consular Body has carefully considered the draft agreement on the implementation of the Chinese Factory Law in the International Settlement. My colleagues want me to reply that they are very sympathetic to the Municipal Council and the Chinese authorities' efforts to find a satisfactory solution to this problem. However, there is one important point, that is, they request that this agreement must have an amendment. It is found that this agreement intends to apply Chinese law to all factories in the Boundary, regardless of their nationality, which will inevitably lead to the abolition of a part of the treaty privileges of countries with consular jurisdiction. However, the Municipal Council should know that it has no right to make such a decision within its authority. Such a step is a matter between the governments of various countries and the Chinese government. Therefore, the Consular Body requests that Your Excellency should strive to obtain an amendment to this draft agreement, clearly stipulating that its provisions can only be applied to factories within the Boundary that are subject to Chinese jurisdiction. On the contrary, that is, it cannot stipulate any words that involve factories of various countries participating in the Municipal Council in the Yangjingbang Regulations as the same inspection steps, etc."

Will Negotiate Again: After receiving the letter from Brenan, Chairman of the Municipal Council, Arnold, summoned Municipal Council Director-General Fessenden to discuss the matter and instructed Fessenden to notify us. Because yesterday was Saturday afternoon, the Municipal Council and the Municipal Government were closed. Today is also a Sunday holiday. Fessenden is now scheduled to meet with Municipal Secretary-General Yu Hongjun tomorrow to continue negotiations. This pending case that has been negotiated for four or five years, just after the draft agreement was discussed and everyone was celebrating that it had been resolved, now the Consular Body has requested to propose amendments, and another wave of twists and turns has occurred.

Haiheng Steamer Stops Selling Tickets to Shantou and Guangdong 107

Whether other ships will stop selling tickets has not yet been decided.

The number of passengers coming to Shanghai from Guangdong in recent days is rare in the past two years. The Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Hai Zhen steamer imported passengers from Shantou and Guangzhou, filling all the cabins. According to people on the ship, the Hai Zhen steamer's ticket revenue this time reached 8,090 yuan, which is a new record after the completion and navigation of the Four New Steamers. Due to the situation, the amount of goods coming from Shantou and Guangdong has been greatly reduced. From Shanghai, except for soybean cakes, there are no other goods to be loaded. Yesterday, the Merchants Steam Navigation Company ordered the new Hai Heng steamer to sail from Shanghai to Nanhua and immediately stop selling tickets from Shanghai to Guangdong and Shantou. It was only allowed to sell tickets from Shanghai to Xiamen and Hong Kong. It is heard that the reason for the Hai Heng's suspension of ticket sales to Guangdong is that the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Committee does not want the Four New Steamers, which were built with Boxer Indemnity funds, to sail into the turbulent Guangdong situation again. If the situation can improve, tickets to Shantou and Guangdong can be sold at any time.

Two Steamships Encounter Peril 108

Hwa Mao Aground at Reef The Hwa Xin Trading Company's "Hwa Mao" steamship, registered at 4,713 tons but capable of carrying 7,000 tons of cargo, is currently sailing around Luzon in the South Seas. Yesterday, the company received a telegram from the "Hwa Mao" stating that at 10:05 PM on the 10th, while sailing in the waters off Luzon, in an area called Calemboyanga, the ship mistakenly strayed from its course due to fog and ran aground on a reef. It was unable to move. Subsequent inspection revealed that the ship's bow was still 60 feet from the reef, so the hull had not yet been damaged or sprung a leak. However, the water depth at the grounding point was only 16 feet, while the ship's draft was 25 feet, leaving the ship unable to move. It could not free itself from the shallows. It is planned to take advantage of the high tide this morning to attempt to reverse off the reef. If this is unsuccessful, arrangements will have to be made to send a ship to rescue, tow, and offload cargo.

Shun An Damaged The Haitong Company's "Shun An" steamship, with a load capacity of 1,455 tons, is currently sailing between ports in the North and South Seas. Yesterday, a telegram from the ship stated that as it was unmooring in Xiamen, the engine had just started when the rear propeller became entangled in a floating drum's iron chain. The engine was quickly shut down, and divers were hired to inspect. It was found that the propeller shaft had been severed, and the iron chain from the floating drum was tightly wrapped around the propeller hub. The ship was unable to sail. Arrangements were immediately made to send a ship to tow the "Shun An" to the Xiamen Naval Shipyard for major repairs, replacement of the propeller, and removal of the chain entangled in the hub. This will result in a delay in the ship's schedule and significant losses.

Salt Merchant Representatives Come to Shanghai to Sign Contract

The Hua Dong News Agency reports that, due to economic panic and slow sales of stored salt, salt merchants in Northern Jiangsu previously sent representatives to Shanghai to request loans from major banks in the city, using the stored salt as collateral, to provide relief. In recent days, they have reached an agreement with the Bank of China to provide a loan of 35 cents per package of salt, with a total loan amount of approximately 3 million yuan. The bank's seven conditions have reportedly been fully accepted by the salt merchants due to their urgent need for funds. The contract is expected to be signed within a few days.

Contract Signed for China Construction Bank Corporation Investment in Chengdu-Chongqing Railway Construction 112

Total Loan Amount of 56 Million National Currency Survey Work Begins, Estimated to Be Completed in Two Years

The Sichuan Provincial Government is preparing to form the Sichuan-Guizhou Railway Company to build the Chengdu-Chongqing Railway. The required funds have been negotiated by Lu Zuofu, Director of the Sichuan Construction Department, and Song Ziliang, General Manager of the China Construction Bank Corporation. It has been decided that the Construction Bank Corporation will invest 56 million yuan. The loan contract has now been formally signed. The Chengdu-Chongqing Railway has begun surveying. The Xin Xin News Agency reporter reported the details as follows:

Organizing the Company Lu Zuofu, Director of the Sichuan Construction Department, prepared a detailed plan for the construction of the Chengdu-Chongqing Railway and consulted with the Ministry of Railways to organize the Sichuan-Guizhou Railway Company to be responsible for the construction. The company's organizational regulations were formally approved by the Executive Yuan's routine meeting on March 21 of this year, stipulating that the total amount of shares would be 20 million yuan, divided into 200,000 shares, with the Ministry of Railways and the Sichuan Provincial Government each recognizing 25,500 shares, and the rest to be raised independently. The company may issue company bonds to supplement the construction funds.

Responsible for Road Construction After Lu Zuofu, Director of the Sichuan Construction Department, prepared the budget and route map for the construction of the Chengdu-Chongqing Railway and submitted them to Zhang Jiaao, Minister of Railways, for approval, the route was determined to first build the main line from Chengdu to Chongqing, and the branch line from Neijiang to Zigong. After completion, other lines will be expanded. It was also decided that the Sichuan-Guizhou Railway Company would be responsible for the construction. The Ministry of Railways has now sent a large number of surveyors to work with the company's surveyors to carry out survey work according to the planned route. Construction is expected to begin in the shortest possible time, and the entire line is expected to be completed and open to traffic within two years.

Loan Signed After the construction budget for the Chengdu-Chongqing Railway was approved by the Ministry of Railways, Director Lu visited Shanghai several times to negotiate investment with Song Ziliang, General Manager of the China Construction Bank Corporation. Song expressed his acceptance in principle and sent personnel to Chongqing to continue negotiating the details. According to reliable information obtained by the Xin Xin News Agency reporter, the investment has become a reality. The China Construction Bank Corporation has decided to invest 56 million yuan. The draft contract has been formally signed, using the Post-Disaster Reconstruction Public Bonds issued by Sichuan Province on April 1, a portion of the Ministry of Railways' third-term public bonds, and the income from the Chengdu-Chongqing Railway after its completion as collateral. The method of disbursement stipulates that payments will be made at any time as required by the project.
