Head of the Nanyang Survey Mission Gao Shiheng Talks About the Mission to the South 114

The Nanyang Commercial Survey Mission is scheduled to depart on July 16, which is a great undertaking for our country to conduct a commercial survey overseas. Gao Shiheng, the head of the mission, told visitors yesterday about the mission to the South as follows: Gao said that with the help of the Nanyang overseas Chinese and the government, the mission to the South consists of fifteen people, representing thirty-seven domestic goods manufacturing factories, and is scheduled to depart on the 16th of this month. The Nanyang overseas Chinese are enthusiastic about the cause of the motherland and often return to the country for surveys. This year, survey missions from Siam, Surabaya, Manila, etc. have visited Shanghai one after another to visit domestic goods factories, and the impression is very good. They believe that domestic goods have made rapid progress recently and should be promoted in various parts of Nanyang. Moreover, the overseas Chinese love the motherland and are very enthusiastic about the promotion of domestic goods. Therefore, at the request of the overseas Chinese, the China National Industries and Foreign Trade Association organized the Nanyang Commercial Survey Mission to go to various parts of Nanyang for exhibitions. Recently, letters have been received from the general chambers of commerce and other overseas Chinese organizations in various parts of Nanyang, all expressing their welcome. Their enthusiasm is truly admirable.

Nanyang has always been known as a wealthy area, and there are more than 5.5 million overseas Chinese, which is a great market. However, the import of domestic goods is still small, which is not enough to meet the consumption of overseas Chinese. In recent years, the domestic industrial circles have also paid great attention to the Nanyang market. The organization of this mission is to publicize the current situation of domestic goods, so that the overseas Chinese in Nanyang can have a full understanding of the outstanding achievements of the domestic industry, and plant a good influence. At the same time, it also opens up a market foundation for the domestic goods industry in various parts of Nanyang, so as to solve the current serious problems of the domestic goods industry. However, in the Nanyang market, neighboring countries often have various survey missions conducting surveys, with the intention of actively implementing the Southward policy and establishing their economic power in Nanyang. Therefore, in addition to conducting commercial surveys, this mission also has complete samples of products from various industries, which will be donated to overseas Chinese in various places. There are more than 300 boxes in quantity, and a domestic goods exhibition will be organized with the local chamber of commerce and overseas Chinese organizations. After the exhibition, a showroom will be set up to display various domestic goods products. In recent years, the trade figures between China and Nanyang have been very small, and neighboring countries in the market are actively expanding their power. The mission of this mission is undoubtedly difficult, but with the guidance of the government and the enthusiasm of the factory circles and the warm welcome from the overseas Chinese in various places, the mission is willing to do its best to be a pioneer for the domestic goods industry. Silk Industry Bank Establishes New Business Guidelines Genuine Cooperation with Jiangsu Bank 118

Replenish Capital Expand Acceptance and Discount Business The Board of Directors Decides to Appoint Lu Zidong as General Manager

The Xin Sheng News Agency reports that the Shanghai Silk Industry Bank was established in September of the 20th year of the Republic (1931) with a capital of 1.2 million yuan. It operates all commercial banking business and also handles savings and trusts. It is a member bank of the Shanghai Banking Association and has successively joined the Bill Exchange and the Joint Reserve Committee. Over the years, the bank's authorities have been able to cater to the financial trends and have taken the lead in advocating a new system of accepting bills of exchange, which has been deeply valued by the financial and industrial and commercial circles. Last winter, in order to expand its business and help the silk industry, the bank submitted a request to Chairman Chiang, ordering the Ministry of Finance to properly plan and replenish the bank's capital. After the Ministry of Finance sent personnel to verify the bank's content, it repeatedly ordered the China, Communications, and Jiangsu Banks to check and handle the matter. After the bank consulted with the authorities of the three banks, a method has now been agreed upon to cooperate genuinely with the Jiangsu Bank. China Communications is willing to be the backing, allocating as much capital as possible to expand various businesses. The bank's chairman, Wang Yansong, proposed and the board of directors passed a resolution to extend an invitation to Lu Zidong, general manager of the Jiangsu Bank, to serve concurrently as the general manager of the bank, in order to achieve thorough cooperation. It is heard that Lu is scheduled to take over immediately. The details are as follows:

The Board of Directors Decides Yesterday, the bank convened a meeting of the board of directors and supervisors, including Directors Yu Zuoting, Wang Boyuan, Feng Zhongqing, Shou Yicheng, Pei Yunqing, Shen Qinzhai, Chen Ziming, Wang Boying, Luo Qinghua, and Supervisor Xu Jilun. They discussed Chairman Wang's proposal to appoint Lu Zidong, general manager of the Jiangsu Bank, to serve concurrently as general manager of the bank, which was unanimously passed. It was also decided to convene a temporary shareholders meeting at 4:00 PM on the 26th of this month to report on the improved business guidelines and the situation of replenishing capital. Warehouses or offices will be established in the silk regions of Jiangsu and Zhejiang to provide as much mortgage lending as possible. The discount business for accepted bills of exchange will also continue to be promoted to benefit industry and commerce. Internal expenses will be reduced as much as possible, all of which will be implemented step by step after General Manager Lu takes office.

A Brief History of Jiangsu Bank The bank is the Jiangsu Provincial Bank. In the first year of the Republic (1912), the provincial government formulated regulations through the provincial assembly to allocate 1 million yuan as capital to establish a head office in Shanghai, with Chen Guangfu as the first general manager. After its establishment, the business developed rapidly. At that time, the banking industry in our country did not know about savings and warehousing business. The bank was the first to organize it, which really opened up the trend. Up to now, twenty-five years later, it has been steadily developing. Last year, the capital was increased to 2 million yuan, and Lu Zidong succeeded as general manager, changing the general management office system to a head office system to save expenses, increase institutions, and promote business. The future is even more promising. At present, in addition to the paid-in capital of 2 million yuan, there are 1.7 million yuan in various public reserves and 23 million yuan in various deposits. The total business volume has reached 38 million yuan. There are currently 33 branches and offices, located throughout Jiangsu Province and the surrounding industrial and commercial centers. In addition to the various statutory businesses of commercial banks, the business includes savings and trusts, and acting as the provincial and county treasury. Since the founding of the Republic, domestic political finance has undergone repeated changes, and financial institutions have risen and fallen accordingly. However, the bank has been able to survive the risks and has never been affected. Its progress may not necessarily be faster than others, so it can withstand the wind without damage. This is all due to the consistent policy of steady progress by successive leaders. At the beginning of its establishment, the bank had already obtained the right to issue banknotes, and printed millions of convertible notes. In the 18th year of the Republic (1929), it voluntarily gave up the right to issue banknotes and burned all the convertible notes to avoid the expansion of local currency and to consolidate the bank's foundation. This alone is enough to show the excellent vision and careful management of the bank's authorities. Its outstanding reputation is not accidental.

A Brief History of Lu Zidong Mr. Lu is a native of Wuxing, Zhejiang. He is 45 years old. He studied in the United States in his early years and obtained a degree. After returning to China, he had outstanding achievements in managing industries. He successively served as the general manager of Changxing Coal Mine Company and the general manager of Lieshan Coal Mine Company. He is currently the chairman and general manager of Dazhong Coal Mine Company. Last year, he was also hired as the general manager of Jiangsu Bank. His careful planning and rapid business progress have increased the total business volume to more than 38 million yuan, and the number of deposits has also increased more than doubled. It shows that Mr. Lu is both experienced and steady. Mr. Lu was newly elected as an executive committee member of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Members Congress and also serves as the director of the Finance Committee and the director of the General Affairs Department.

Prospects for Silk Industry Bank The Silk Industry Bank was established not long ago, and the total amount of deposits once reached 3.5 million yuan. The bank's authorities are also striving to adapt to the modern financial trends. The bank's organization has basically been established and has been well received by the public. However, due to limited funds, it has not been able to fully expand its business. Now that it has the genuine cooperation of Jiangsu Bank, and China Communications Bank is willing to be the backing, the capital will be replenished and the credit will be consolidated. The bank's reputation will inevitably increase day by day. With Lu Zidong serving as general manager, earnestly rectifying the bank's affairs and expanding its business, the bank's prospects are even brighter, and business progress can be guaranteed.

Laogezhilu Old Zhengli Dyeing Shop Forced by Police to Pay Business License Fee

According to Guomin News Agency, Old Zhengli Dyeing Shop, a member of the Tenth District Branch of the Second Special District Citizens Association in this city, was investigated by the Chinese and foreign detectives of the French Concession Municipal Council at the end of last month regarding a business license. The shop replied to the detectives that businesses on this road have never had such a business donation. The detectives then left a paper written in Western language. Unexpectedly, at 2:00 PM on the 6th of this month, detectives from the Yuandang Road police station were sent to the shop, saying the police station had an important case and to go quickly. The shop sent a staff member, and the police station said that failure to obtain a health permit would result in a fine of ten yuan. Because the staff member did not have any money at the time, he was detained for four hours. The district branch sent a letter to the French Concession Taxpayers Association yesterday requesting negotiations. The original text is recorded below: "To the honorable sir, according to the letter from our member, Xu Huijun of the Old Zhengli Dyeing Shop, at the end of June this year, Chinese and foreign detectives from the French Concession Municipal Council inquired at our shop whether we had a business license. Our shop replied that all businesses on this road (Hague Road) have never donated for such a license, and our shop does not need to make an exception to donate. The Municipal Council staff then suddenly asked if there was a health permit, and we replied that our shop is a branch, and there is no machinery installed inside, nor is there washing or dyeing. All items sent for dyeing by customers are sent to the main store for washing and dyeing every day. It is purely a receiving and sending operation, and there is no obstacle to hygiene. According to reason, there is no need to donate a health permit. The staff member did not say anything and left a paper written in Western language. Our shop thought that the facts had been clearly stated and there would be no problem. Unexpectedly, at 2:00 PM on the 6th of this month, a patrolman and a detective from the Beidang Road police station came to the shop and said that the police station had an important case and asked to go quickly for questioning. Our shop often replied that it would be there after a short break, but the patrolman and detective were unbearably fierce, claiming that they must go immediately. Our shop thought that since we had not broken the law, it would not hurt to go for questioning. We sent a staff member to the police station. Unexpectedly, after entering the police station, the police chief said that the Municipal Council ordered a fine of ten yuan for not obtaining a health permit. Our shop staff member explained the previous situation and gave further explanations, but the police chief refused to accept it and forcibly detained our shop staff member in the police station for four hours. It was already 7:00 PM when the deputy police chief told our shop staff member, 'If you don't pay the fee today, I will send a patrolman to guard you overnight.' Such harsh measures are rare. Our shop was forced to pay a deposit of ten yuan in national currency and obtained a temporary receipt issued by the deputy police chief as evidence before being released. We thought that the Municipal Council had sent someone to investigate beforehand, and the facts were very clear. Why did they arbitrarily impose a fine? And the police station used methods to lure our shop staff member to the police station. After repeated explanations, not only did they not listen, but they forcibly detained him for four hours and wanted to send a patrolman to guard him overnight. If we had not temporarily paid the ten yuan deposit, how long would we have been unreasonably detained before being allowed to regain freedom? Such arbitrary arrests of the innocent, darkness without daylight, what is the meaning of human rights? What is the meaning of law? At this time of economic downturn, the unreasonable oppression our shop suffers is small, and the protection of all citizens is great. For this reason, we have no choice but to write to your association, requesting you to forward this to the Chinese Taxpayers Association and argue with the Municipal Council to recover the ten yuan in French currency that has been paid to the police station, and to ensure that the same thing does not happen again in the future, in order to relieve the difficulties of businesses and maintain human rights." After checking, the member operates a business at 1169AB Hague Road, and there is indeed no machinery or dyeing inside. Since it does not hinder hygiene, there is no need to donate a health permit in principle. However, the Municipal Council ordered the police station to impose a fine for no reason and forcibly detained the shop's staff member for more than four hours, and there was a tendency to continue the detention, which is far from legal. This matter involves the police station abusing its power and citizens being detained for no reason. It is reasonable to write to your association to negotiate with the Municipal Council to recover the ten yuan in national currency that has been paid, severely punish the police station's abuse of power, and ensure that the same thing does not happen again in the future, in order to maintain justice and promote human rights. This is for the public good. Respectfully, the Tenth District Branch of the Second Special District City Federation of the French Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association.

Tang Hai'an Will Return North; Guangdong's Adoption of the Silver Dollar System Shelved 121

Due to Difficulties in Transferring Silver to Central Custody

Tang Shoumin's Trip South Decidedly Canceled

The Central Government, in order to unify the currency system, had sent Tang Hai'an, Senior Advisor to the Ministry of Finance and Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, again with Feng Rui, Director of the Provincial Department of Agriculture and Forestry, to the South to discuss everything in detail. Subsequently, due to the Guangdong Province's difficulties in transferring silver to central custody, Tang's trip yielded no results. He will return to the North in a few days. At the same time, the southward trips of Tang Shoumin and Bei Zuyi have also been confirmed to be canceled. The reporter from Shenshi News Agency specially visited relevant parties yesterday to find out the details:

The Process of Two Discussions on System Change

According to a certain gentleman in financial circles familiar with this issue, since the Ministry of Finance implemented the currency system policy in January of last year, following central laws, all provinces have successively followed suit, so foreign exchange is stable and convenient for both Chinese and foreigners. The Guangdong Provincial authorities, due to the holding of the silver coin system, have not yet adopted the silver dollar system. The Ministry of Finance believes that the national currency system should be unified, so in April of this year, it sent Tang Hai'an, Senior Advisor and Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, to Guangdong to negotiate everything with the provincial financial authorities. The Guangdong provincial financial authorities, together with banking experts, conducted a special study and decided on a method, which Tang took to Beijing, and Feng Rui, Director of the Department of Agriculture and Forestry, accompanied him to Beijing to discuss everything. A concrete method was also drafted, and Tang was sent back to Guangdong with Feng Rui to handle it. This is the process of the Ministry of Finance's two decisions to discuss the adoption of the silver dollar system with the Guangdong provincial authorities.

Negotiations on Silver Sales Shelved

After Tang and Feng arrived in Hong Kong, Tang initially stayed in Hong Kong temporarily, while Feng immediately returned to the province. Later, it was heard that the transfer of silver to central custody had not been agreed upon, and the Guangdong provincial authorities believed that the transfer of silver to central custody was difficult to handle. They automatically sent personnel from the Legal Tender Committee to Hong Kong to build a large silver warehouse to store Guangdong's silver reserves, so they decided to stop the transfer to the central government and stated that if the central government insisted on unifying the currency system, it would have to find another appropriate method, which Guangdong would certainly accept. Therefore, although Tang had this trip, in fact, he may not have had direct negotiations with the Guangdong provincial authorities, and turned back to Hong Kong. At the same time, recent reports have said that the Guangdong provincial authorities have prepared to sell the stored silver to foreign merchants and have transported a large number of them to Hong Kong for deposit in foreign banks. Judging from this, the issue of Guangdong's adoption of the silver dollar system seems to have been shelved for the time being.

Guangdong Officials Once Came to Beijing and Shanghai to Investigate

It was also learned that the Guangdong Provincial Legal Tender Committee recently sent Secretary Zhou Shuchang to Beijing, Shanghai, and other places to investigate the financial situation and planned to form Guangdong Provincial Legal Tender branches, but the results were not very satisfactory. He returned to Guangdong at the end of last week to report to the authorities, so the Guangdong Province's recent decision to sell silver and deposit it in foreign banks in Hong Kong may have been determined by this.

Tang and Bei Are Not Going; Hai'an Will Return

According to reliable information, Tang Shoumin, manager of the Bank of Communications, and Bei Zuyi, manager of the Shanghai branch of the Bank of China, who were sent by the Ministry of Finance to Guangdong Province to assist in discussing the adoption of the silver dollar system and reorganizing foreign exchange, have now decided to cancel their trip south because the issue has entered a state of being shelved. They will decide after the Ministry of Finance decides on a direction. As for Tang Hai'an, who was tasked with going to Guangdong to discuss the adoption of the silver dollar system, he has returned to Hong Kong from Guangdong to await transportation, so that he can return to the North to report on his mission as soon as possible, as this trip has not yielded results.

Concessions Treat Opium Offenders According to the Anti-Opium and Anti-Drug Regulations 122

The anti-opium and anti-drug regulations promulgated by the central government have been in effect for a long time. Due to special circumstances in the concessions of this city, although the special district courts have handled opium and drug cases in accordance with these regulations, the police, who have the power to prosecute, still filed charges against opium and drug offenders based on the opium crime provisions of the criminal law that had been abolished, resulting in the judiciary, prosecution, and investigation each acting independently, which affected the dignity of our country's judiciary. Although the foreigners had previously expressed their willingness to comply with the new regulations, they have not yet been implemented. Now that we have added a "possession" clause to the regulations, and after repeated consultations with the Public Concession Municipal Council, the Council has now fully understood and sincerely assisted our country's anti-opium policy, so that the concession area will not become a haven for opium addicts in the future and be criticized by the world. From yesterday, the opium and drug offenders sent by the police stations to the First Special District Local Court for interrogation have all been prosecuted according to the Shanghai Anti-Opium Regulations.

Debate Concludes in Seduction and Abandonment Case Demanding Huge Compensation 123

Zheng Shiyue Demands $144,000

Chen Mingxun Proves Playing and Cohabitation

Zheng Shiyue, a Ningbo woman who is now twenty years old, was a salesperson at the Great American Tobacco Company. Recently, she hired lawyer Wang Liangqing to sue Chen Mingxun, the owner of the Rixin Chang Foreign Goods Store at No. 29, Lane 240, Edward Road, in the First Special District Court for seduction and abandonment, and attached a civil suit demanding $144,000 for living expenses. The court had already summoned each party once, as reported in this newspaper on the 3rd of this month. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Huang Daxi held a continued hearing. Zheng Shiyue was absent due to illness and was only represented by her lawyer Wang. Chen Mingxun arrived in court with his defense lawyer Wu Linkun and presented a defense, stating that the plaintiff Zheng Shiyue was a prostitute at No. 82 Wufu Lane. In October of the 23rd year of the Republic, the defendant was invited by friends Cao Shourong and Shen Xingu to go to play, and the defendant also invited friends to play mahjong. The plaintiff became increasingly close to the defendant because of this and coaxed him in every way, so they cohabited, but there was no intention to marry the plaintiff as his wife or to take her as a member of his family. He also did not know that she already had a husband and did not force her to divorce her husband. Furthermore, regarding the legal provisions cited by the plaintiff, Article 240, Paragraph 2 of the criminal law for seducing a person with a spouse to leave their family, and Article 293, the first half of the abandonment crime, the crime in Article 240, Paragraph 2, must be prosecuted by the husband according to the Criminal Procedure Law, and the statute of limitations for prosecution is six months. The statute of limitations has also passed. Furthermore, Article 1 of the new criminal law stipulates that the punishment of an act is limited to the law that expressly stipulates it at the time of the act, that is, according to what the plaintiff said, its time was the 23rd year of the Republic, and the old criminal law was still applicable at that time, but the old criminal law did not have a provision like the crime in Article 240, Paragraph 2 of the new criminal law. Since the law has no express provision, it should not be punished. Furthermore, regarding Article 293 of the criminal law, the elements of the crime of abandonment require the abandoned person to be old, young, or disabled. The plaintiff is in her prime and is not a person without the ability to save herself. Furthermore, the plaintiff's identity is a secret prostitute, so the complaint does not conform to the facts of law and there is no reason. The complaint should be rejected, and a counterclaim for false accusation should be filed. Judge Huang questioned Chen Mingxun and ordered the lawyers of both parties to begin the debate, then announced the conclusion of the debate and scheduled the verdict for the afternoon of the 16th.

After the Opening of the Sujia Road, Transshipment Method for Joint Transportation on Two Roads 129

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways, in order to facilitate the operation of vehicles and reduce the mileage of empty cars, given that the Sujia Railway will soon be opened on the 15th of this month, have now decided that from the date of the opening of the Sujia Railway, all joint transportation vehicles on the two roads and other roads from Zhengyi Station on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway and stations east of Zhengyi Station to Songjiang Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway and stations east of Songjiang Station, or from Songjiang Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway and stations east of Songjiang Station to Zhengyi Station on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway and stations east of Zhengyi Station, will be transshipped at Maigen Road Station. All joint transportation vehicles on the two roads and other roads from Weiting Station on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway and stations west of Weiting Station to Shihudang Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway and stations west of Shihudang Station, or from Shihudang Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway and stations west of Shihudang Station to Weiting Station on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway and stations west of Weiting Station, will be transshipped at Wuxian Station and Jiaxing Station via the Sujia Railway.

Niu Huaijin Sues Puqing Hospital; Defendant Presents Three Witnesses 132

Zhang Fengqi, a doctor at Guangdong Road Puqing Hospital, and his brother Zhang Fengshi, were recently sued by Niu Huaijin from Anhui in the First Special District Court for fraudulently obtaining property and causing injury through negligence, and attached a civil suit demanding compensation for damages of 15,600 yuan. The First Special District Court had already summoned each party once, as detailed in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Tan Xinzhen held a continued hearing in the eighth criminal court. Chen Tingrui, the defense lawyer for the defendants Zhang Fengqi and Zhang Fengshi, began by stating that the defendant had previously submitted a registration book, and the plaintiff attacked it, saying that it was altered from a daily register, so today he specially brought the daily register to the case as proof. Furthermore, three witnesses were present in court today. One, Guo Kechen, is the gatekeeper of Yuqing Lane, Xixin Bridge, proving that the plaintiff Niu Huaijin previously opened the Huiren Hospital at No. 8 in the lane, and fled due to owing several months of rent. There are also two witnesses, named Chuan Jinsheng and Wang Hongtai. These two witnesses can prove that on December 23 of last year, they saw the plaintiff's eyes were already blind and his wife helped him to Puqing Hospital for treatment, because the two witnesses were also seeing a doctor at the time. The three witnesses were immediately summoned to court to provide evidence. The defendant Zhang Fengshi stated that the plaintiff not only opened the Huiren Hospital in Yuqing Lane, but also opened a hospital at the original site of the Shanghai Porridge Restaurant in the Oriental Hotel. Niu Huaijin denied ever opening a hospital, saying that the house at No. 8 Yuqing Lane was indeed rented by him, but the Huiren Hospital was opened by a friend, etc. Judge Tan believed that the case still needed to be investigated and adjourned the hearing to a later date.

French Concession Police Department Declares Appeal in Gu Zhuxuan et al. Case 134

Believing the Original Verdict Violated the Law; First Declaring Appeal, Now Drafting Reasons

Gu Zhuxuan, former owner of the Tianchan Stage and president of the Jianghuai Shanghai Fellow Townsmen Association from Yancheng, and Wang Xinggao, a Funing native who had previously served in the military and police, were reported by Zhao Guangfu, the perpetrator in the assassination of Tang Jiapeng, as instigators of Tang's murder. The French Police Department arrested Gu and Wang one after another and sent them to the Second Special District Court for a verdict. Wang Xinggao was sentenced to life imprisonment and permanent deprivation of civil rights, and Gu Zhuxuan was sentenced to 15 years of imprisonment and 10 years of deprivation of civil rights. Because Gu and Wang did not accept the verdict, they appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court one after another. The trial concluded, and the verdict was announced on the 26th of last month, acquitting Gu Zhuxuan and Wang Xinggao. Wang Xinggao was allowed to be released on bail of 10,000 yuan during the appeal period and completed the bail procedures the day before yesterday, regaining his freedom. However, because Gu was sentenced to eight months of imprisonment in the case of smoking opium while in custody, he is still detained in the detention center. After the verdicts in the two cases were delivered by the police from the Third Branch of the High Court on the 3rd of this month, Guo Tang Youmei, the family member and younger sister of the victim Tang Jiapeng, learned of it and immediately requested the French Police Department to file an appeal. The Police Department accepted the request and carefully studied the reasons for the verdicts in the two cases, believing that there were violations of the law. Because the 10-day appeal deadline was approaching, they first drafted a statement of appeal and submitted it to the Third Branch of the High Court, declaring that they would appeal the two cases of Gu and Wang. Legal advisers and lawyers of the Police Department are currently studying and drafting detailed reasons for the appeal.

Serial Killer and Repeat Offender Robber, Gu You Ting, Sentenced to Death 135

His Face Turned Pale Upon Hearing the Verdict, Official Informed Him of His Right to Appeal

Gu You Ting, a 34-year-old man from Shaoxing, had previously been convicted of multiple robberies. The First Special District Court sentenced him to ten years in prison. After being paroled in the summer of the 23rd year of the Republic [1934], at around 11 AM on August 1st of that year, he alone, armed, robbed Liu Ziyou, a rent collector for the Action Benefit Bank on Malang Road in the French Concession, of over 600 yuan in collected rent. He fled east along Kangti Road. Detectives heard the alarm and gave chase. Gu opened fire in resistance, mortally wounding a passerby, Jiang Jinshan (from Shaoxing, a houseboy). Jiang died instantly. Gu fled to the Shunyang Li entrance on Caishi Road, where he was finally apprehended by the detectives. However, during the emergency, he threw the stolen money into the road, where it was all picked up by passersby and children. Only a pistol and an original robber's check were found on Gu's person. He was sent to the Second Special Court. The police department initiated a public prosecution for both robbery and murder. After interrogation and judgment, Gu was sentenced to seven years for robbery and death for murder, to be carried out immediately. Gu appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court, which changed the sentence to life imprisonment. Dissatisfied, the prosecutor of the Third Branch of the High Court appealed to the Supreme Court, which ordered the original judgment overturned and the case returned to the Third Branch of the High Court for a retrial. This case has been repeatedly heard and examined by the High Court, with witnesses summoned. Yesterday morning at 10 AM, Zhu Huanbiao, acting presiding judge of the Third Branch of the High Court, accompanied by assessors Liao and Fan, came to the Third Tribunal, ordered the accused Gu to be brought to court, briefly questioned him, and then announced the verdict. The main text: The original judgment is reversed. Gu You Ting is sentenced to death as a serial killer and repeat offender.

Municipal Council Orders Removal of Shantytowns, Residents Surround Detectives 136

Result: Extension Granted, But Must Relocate by the 15th; Organizing Shantytown United Association for all Locations in the International Settlement

Yesterday, the Public Works Department of the Shanghai International Settlement sent detectives to evict the shantytown dwellers in the Eastern District. The shantytown dwellers surrounded the detectives with chamber pots and brooms. The following are the detailed findings of a reporter from the New Voice News Agency.

Total Exceeds Ten Thousand

The shantytowns in the Eastern District of the Public International Settlement are scattered throughout Pingliang Road, Yulin Road, Qiwupu Road, Qiqihar Road, Peikai'er Road, Helong Road, Meizhou Road, Hejian Road, Ningguo Road, Linqing Road, Xihu Road, Zhaoyang Road, Huade Road, Tangshan Road, Kunming Road, Zhoushan Road, Gelan Road, Liping Road, Longjiang Road, Funing Road, and other locations, totaling approximately ten thousand households.

History of the Shantytowns

These shantytown dwellers are mostly coolies from Jiangbei who came to Shanghai to make a living. Because rent is expensive, they built thatched sheds on desolate lands. Some of these lands are barren wastelands, some pay land rent to the landowners, and some belong to the Public Works Department. In the past, because they were in rural areas, neither the landowners nor the Public Works Department cared. However, as the market has become more prosperous in recent years, the Public Works Department attempted to add house numbers two years ago to increase the revenue from patrolmen's fees, but this was opposed and not implemented.

Limited Time for Relocation

Recently, the Public Works Department has repeatedly sent personnel to inspect and numbered the shantytown doors with green paint, intending to re-number the houses. At the same time, a notice was issued to the shantytowns west of Lan Road, stating: "Notice: These thatched sheds are located west of Meizhou Road and north of Helong Road, Title Deed No. 7842. This Bureau orders these shantytown dwellers to relocate by July 11, 1936, otherwise, they will be demolished. This is hereby notified." For shantytowns east of Lan Road, the deadline for relocation is August 8.

Armed Eviction

Yesterday morning at 8 AM, the Yulin Road Police Station and the Andong Road Branch of the Public Works Department sent over fifty armed Chinese and foreign detectives to the Yanshan Road and Qiqihar Road area, ordering the shantytown dwellers to relocate immediately, saying that if they did not move, they would be forcibly demolished. The shantytown dwellers pleaded for an extension and sent people to report to other locations, requesting assistance.

Surrounded by the Crowd

By 9 AM, shantytown dwellers from various locations, women carrying chamber pots, children carrying chamber pots and washcloths, and men carrying brooms, gathered over two thousand people, surrounding the fifty-odd detectives. The women stacked chamber pots around the detectives, forming a sort of wall. There were a large number of people shouting and cursing incessantly. The two sides were deadlocked. It was quite a farce.

Extension of Five Days

At that time, the foreign head of the detectives, helpless, after consulting with the crowd, told the shantytown dwellers that a five-day extension would be granted until the 15th (Wednesday), but they had to relocate within this period, otherwise, one hundred and twenty detectives and British soldiers would be sent to forcibly demolish the buildings. The shantytown dwellers considered the matter temporarily resolved and dispersed, and the detectives also left in disappointment.

Request for Negotiation

In addition to requesting negotiations with the Citizens' Association the day before, the shantytown dwellers requested He Dekui of the Public Works Department to be exempted from relocation, but this was not granted. They also petitioned the Taxpayers' Association for relief, and Secretary Tao Leqin received them, promising to handle the matter according to regulations. At the same time, they separately submitted petitions to the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Municipal Government, and the Social Affairs Bureau, requesting protest. They planned to submit further petitions to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for relief. Furthermore, shantytown dwellers in the Western and Northern Districts of the concession, feeling sympathy for their plight, sent personnel to express their condolences yesterday. It has also been decided to organize the Shanghai International Settlement Shantytown United Association to conduct negotiations.

For Life. The robbery portion remains at seven years, to be carried out immediately. Upon hearing the verdict of death, Gu's face immediately turned pale, he became stunned, and said nothing. The official informed him that if he did not agree with the verdict, he could still appeal according to law. Then, the bailiffs took the prisoner down and sent him back to the detention center.

Water Level in Hankou and Wuhu Suddenly Rises Again 138

Customs Adds Water Level Markings

The water levels at various ports along the Yangtze River, including Hankou, Jiujiang, and Wuhu, have risen again. Wuhu, in particular, has seen the sharpest increase. A reporter from the Datong News Agency has obtained the following information from the customs:

River Water Rises Again

The water levels at various ports along the Yangtze River, including Hankou, Jiujiang, Anqing, and Wuhu, have risen sharply since the first day of this month. By the fourth, they had begun to recede slightly. However, yesterday's customs report on the Hankou water level for the seventh showed it to be 30 feet 8 inches (compared to only 30 feet 5 inches on the fourth). The Wuhu water level report for the same day showed it to be 22 feet 9 inches (compared to only 22 feet 7 inches on the fourth). Thus, the water level is rising again.

Added Markings

Because the Yangtze River water level is rising, the customs attaches great importance to navigation facilities. Recently, water level markings have been added to the Hanjin Pass waterway between Hankou and Yuezhou. The markings consist of a white cylindrical pole topped with a black spherical basket and a non-rated red fixed light, called the Hanjin Pass Water Level Light Buoy.

Opium Addicts Eager to Quit, Municipal Hospitals Unable to Accommodate 140

Since the Shanghai Municipal Police Department was ordered to enforce the ban on opium, active publicity and strict enforcement have aroused the awareness of opium addicts. After the start of this registration campaign, the department expanded its publicity efforts and detailed the benefits and harms, which further attracted the attention of opium addicts. Therefore, in recent days, there has been an endless stream of people applying to the department for assistance in quitting. However, the municipal hospitals are already full and unable to accommodate them. As a result, dozens of opium addicts who applied to quit have been turned away daily because they could not be admitted. According to the department's statistics, from the start of opium addict registration in July of last year to June of this year, the Shanghai Municipal Huna Hospital cured 2,878 opium addicts (from April of last year to July of this year). The Shanghai Municipal Hubei Hospital cured 4,154 people. The Municipal Criminal Drug Rehabilitation Center cured 1,029 people (from September of last year to June of this year). The Municipal Temporary Drug Rehabilitation Center cured 866 people. The designated hospitals that also handle opium cessation cured 883 people. The non-designated hospitals cured 1,098 people. The total is 10,988 people.

Zhu Yakui from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Zhang Dafu from the Social Affairs Bureau, and Sun Mingqi from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce attended to provide guidance. Qiu Chunshan, Gu Songmao, Wang Bingyan, Zhou Jinyuan, and Qin Jianzhou were elected as Standing Committee members. The Standing Committee members then mutually elected Qiu Chunshan as the Chairman of the Committee. After the elections, the members dined together and dispersed.

Formed Welfare Association, Requested Assistance

Zhang Mingzhi and Zhou Weigao, the general representatives of the rickshaw pullers, and the contractors sent a letter yesterday to the Rickshaw Merchants' Guild, stating: "Regarding the presentation, for the sake of relieving the rickshaw pullers, the representatives, based on the Central Government's circular of 1934 and the plan drafted by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, initiated the Shanghai Rickshaw Pullers' Welfare Association. On the morning of March 31st of this year, the inaugural meeting of the founders was held at the Xiaoximen Juvenile Lecture Hall in Nanshi, with hundreds of people in attendance. The Municipal Party Headquarters sent a special representative, Zhu Yangwu, to attend and provide guidance. At the meeting, it was resolved to organize the Shanghai Rickshaw Pullers' Welfare Association, and Zhang Zhenshan, Zhu Deyao, Wang Degao, and the other five people were elected as the chairmen of the five districts' preparation committees. Later, in order to divide the work and cooperate to improve efficiency, the organizers of each district nominated seven preparatory committee members each, totaling thirty-five people, to form the preparatory committee and jointly take responsibility for the progress. The list of preparatory committee members from each district was reported to the Social Affairs Bureau for record, and opinion letters of the welfare association were prepared and submitted to the party and government agencies of this city for reference. Subsequently, the Rickshaw Pullers' Association sent representatives, Zhou Weigao and others, to the party and government agencies to request guidance in organizing the association to support the coolies, and they were all adopted for discussion and handling. Now, the preparatory committee members have made considerable progress after several months of planning. However, without capital, it is impossible to proceed. The Welfare Association is purely a relief organization, and its funds cannot be obtained from the rickshaw pullers themselves, in order to conform with the main purpose. Moreover, now, in the middle of the hot summer, epidemics are prevalent. The rickshaw pullers toil under the scorching sun, working hard and struggling to make a living. If they unfortunately contract an epidemic, the misery is indescribable. Therefore, relief is urgently needed to prolong their lives. The representatives, although exhausted and heartbroken, are powerless and can only call for responsibility. Under compulsion, we hereby submit this to your association, requesting that you act in the spirit of mutual assistance, immediately raise funds to assist in the good cause and meet the urgent needs. Otherwise, if we delay and if someone else has ulterior motives and takes over the planning, we fear that your association will regret it too late. Now, we are pleased to attend the first Executive Committee meeting of your association and request that you submit it to the meeting for discussion, quickly pass it, and implement it. Then, it will not only benefit the rickshaw pullers. We cannot express the urgency of our request and await your orders."

Comprehensive Physical Examination: Statistics on Health and Disease 147

Published by the Hongqiao Sanitarium in Western Shanghai

Lung Disease Accounts for 44 Percent

The Hongqiao Sanitarium in Shanghai announced the statistics of the comprehensive physical examinations of citizens last month, stating that the hospital, in order to enable the general public to understand their own health status, improve their living conditions, and achieve the purpose of preventing diseases and early treatment, has added a comprehensive physical examination department. The monthly statistical report is as follows: A total of 64 citizens went to the hospital for examinations, with ages ranging from 20 to 40 years old, totaling 42 people, accounting for 65 percent. The youngest was 7 years old, and the oldest was 63 years old. The most common places of origin were Jiangsu and Zhejiang, accounting for 65 percent, followed by Guangdong and Fujian, accounting for 22 percent. The most common occupations were education and business, accounting for 69 percent. Women who were housewives also accounted for 19 percent of those examined, showing that women have also begun to pay attention to their daily health status. In terms of diseases, 28 people were found to have lung disease, accounting for 44 percent of the total. Among them, 25 percent had active pulmonary tuberculosis. The most noteworthy point is that the examinees had no symptoms. In addition, 12 people were found to have aortic and cardiac dilation, accounting for 19 percent, half of whom were over 40 years old. Several cases of droplet-like small hearts were also found. Furthermore, there were many cases of intestinal parasites, cystitis, syphilis, anemia, etc., found as a result of the examinations. The most noteworthy point is that the hospital's blood sedimentation rate test showed that the sedimentation rate was drastically rapid in the first and second hour for active pulmonary tuberculosis, renal tuberculosis, and syphilis, which was completely consistent with the results of other X-ray examinations, etc. It is worthy of being praised as the most useful supplementary diagnostic method. According to the average life expectancy of people in various countries in the world, Denmark is 61, Japan is 42, and China is only 30. Japan and China are of the same race and culture, but the average life expectancy and the strength of the country are almost proportional. It can be seen that daily hygiene not only affects the health of individuals, but also affects the strength of the country and the nation. Since the hospital began performing examinations last month, celebrities from all walks of life, such as Zhu Shaoping, Wang Xiaolai, Cai Jingjun, and Zhao Guanlan, have all visited the hospital, which is a good sign of promoting national health in our country.

Father and Son Quarrel, Jump into River to Commit Suicide 151

Xue Guanhai, a local resident living on a rice-shaking boat in Henan Dong Lane, Changqiao Town, Hunan-Zhe Road, Shanghai, is nearly fifty years old and has two sons. The eldest, Jin Gen, is twenty-two years old. In March of this year, he married a Miss Xi from Xijiatang nearby through a matchmaker. Jin Gen usually worked on the boat as well. However, the day before yesterday, the father and son had a quarrel over a trivial matter. After being scolded, Jin Gen suddenly had the idea of ending his life. The day before yesterday, the boat loaded rice from Sijing to Shanghai. While sailing on the Huangpu River outside Longhua Mouth, Jin Gen took advantage of people's inattention and jumped into the river to commit suicide. Guanhai rushed to save him, but it was too late. It is now known that Jin Gen's body was recovered by a lifeboat on the Bund outside the South City. His family has been notified to identify and collect the body.

Dangerous Incidents in Factories in the Public Concession in June 153

According to a report from the Factory Section of the Public Works Department, a total of 175 industrial and occupational accidents occurred in the Public Concession in June, resulting in 11 deaths and 10 injuries to women. The causes of the above incidents are generally clear in 165 cases. Investigations and instructions for handling were carried out in 106 cases. Regarding the above dangerous incidents, if classified by industry, there were 55 injuries in the machinery and metal manufacturing industry, with 6 deaths; 13 injuries in the construction industry, with 1 death; 12 injuries in the chemical industry, with 1 death; and 17 injuries in the textile industry, with 2 deaths. If analyzed by cause, 40 dangerous incidents were related to electrical machinery, but fortunately, there were no deaths. There were 16 burn injuries, with 5 deaths; 7 electrical injuries, with 1 death; 17 injuries from falling from heights, with 3 deaths; and 33 injuries from falling objects, but no fatalities.

Records of the World Games Delegation's Journey 167

Strength Assessment

Regarding the strength of our athletes and the prospects for participating in this grand event, I have had several detailed conversations with several coaches over the past two days.

In track and field and swimming, although our results have improved rapidly in the last two years, there is still a considerable gap compared to the top athletes from various countries. I asked Mr. Ma Dehan what hopes he had for our athletes. He simply shook his head. If we must place some hope on one or two athletes, then it would naturally be Fu Baolu in the pole vault and Wu Bixian in the high jump. Baolu has achieved heights of over 4 meters, while the United States and Japan have five or six athletes who jump 4.30 meters. However, Baolu has a very strong fighting spirit and may be able to put up a fight at the competition. Bixian has a strength of 1.90 meters; the champion of the last World Games only jumped 1.97 meters, so let's see how he performs. In short, Mr. Ma's intention is that we should not be discouraged or ashamed by the inability to score points but should gain more experience and stimulation from participating, so that our country's sports can move to a new stage in the future.

According to Coach Dong Shouyi, our basketball players are very strong, but the participating countries are probably not weak either. The United States is widely recognized as being sure to win the championship, and the strength of South American countries and Canada is also formidable. This is because basketball originated in the YMCA, and South America and Canada have a long history of organizing the YMCA. In other words, they have been promoting basketball for a long time, and we are probably not yet their match. As for European countries, basketball has not been promoted for long, but their physiques are very strong. Since they have registered for this event, they must have been actively training for a long time, and their strength should not be underestimated. Therefore, our prospects are not optimistic. The only hope is that our team members can show their fighting spirit, play more games, and gain more experience. The order of the basketball competition has not yet been arranged and will only be known after arriving in Germany. We certainly hope to encounter a European team first. As for our lineup, it has not yet been decided and will be adapted to the situation, selecting players to fight. Mr. Dong has a plan in his mind regarding the deployment of the lineup.

In terms of Chinese martial arts, we have a total of nine representatives, but they are there for demonstration purposes, not for competition. When the reporter was in Shanghai, he met Mr. Feierhaosi, the China representative of the German Haitong News Agency. He had seen our representatives' performance and was very surprised and praised them. According to him, this visit to Germany will definitely cause a sensation, and after the Berlin performance, many other cities may invite them to perform. I told our athletes this news, and everyone was very excited and happy.

The four boxing representatives sent by the 32nd Army are generally not highly regarded. People assume that once they step onto the world stage, they will be beaten with bloody noses and fall to the ground. In fact, such a view is wrong. It is said that Commander Shang Zhen's promotion of sports in the army for only two years has not only greatly improved the soldiers' interest and knowledge but also produced great practical effects. For example, when they train soldiers to swim, there was a time when they encountered a large river while suppressing bandits, and the soldiers, having been trained, swam across the river to pursue and suppress them. They practice polo, which has resulted in all cavalrymen having excellent horsemanship. Even boxing, when two people fight each other, even if they are knocked to the ground, they must continue to resist as long as they can get up. This spirit of fighting to the last breath is of great significance to the entire army. Therefore, we should not take it lightly that these four athletes are sent this time. The strength of these four athletes is not very weak. They do not want to win any championships but only hope to gain some experience and increase the interest and skills of all soldiers in boxing.

Four representatives were also sent for race walking. Their results are not far from the world's top athletes, and maybe they will be a dark horse in this event.

The three weightlifting representatives have been training very diligently since boarding the ship, maintaining the nature of strongmen. Their results are not far from the world's top players either. It is of course difficult to predict whether they have any hope at this time.

The football team is still playing matches along the way and has not yet suffered a defeat, but when they encounter machine-like teams from Europe and South America, the chances of success are slim.

Now, the opening of the Games is approaching day by day. After the entire team arrives in Berlin, there will be a week of practice opportunities. The spirit of the entire team is very excited, and the fighting spirit is also very strong, which is reassuring to those who care about them at home.

Arrival in Singapore

This morning (the 2nd), I was awakened from my sleep by the noise. Everyone woke up especially early because we were about to arrive in Singapore. When I went to the deck, I saw many small islands on the sea surface. These were the long-admired Nanyang Islands. The seawater changed from deep blue to turquoise, calm and waveless. The mail ship moved forward slowly, showing a kind of peaceful atmosphere.

Around nine o'clock, Singapore appeared before our eyes. Many tall Western-style buildings were arranged on the seashore like a long snake, exceptionally neat. Many giant ships were parked at the docks extending into the water, fully demonstrating that it is a transportation hub between Europe and Asia.

The ship docked around ten o'clock. Hundreds of welcoming overseas Chinese stood on the pier, all wearing white clothes and holding small party and national flags in their hands. When the mail ship approached, they shouted loudly, "Long live the Republic of China!" We leaned on the ship's rails and responded with enthusiastic cheers. The scene was truly exciting to the extreme.

Customs gave preferential treatment to the delegation, exempting them from passport inspection procedures. However, because we had to wait for all the other passengers to have their passports checked before disembarking, the time was delayed until 11:30.

The very bright sun suddenly turned cloudy as everyone was preparing to disembark. A gust of wind brought heavy rain, just like when we disembarked in Hong Kong. The delegation and the rain are probably very related.

After the rain, the climate in Singapore was very cool, not at all like the tropical climate we imagined. It is said that Singapore is very cool in the morning, with the highest temperature at noon only reaching 92 degrees, and dropping to over 50 degrees at night, all year round. Compared to the climate in Beijing and Shanghai, it is much better.

After disembarking, the entire group divided into dozens of cars, large and small, and, accompanied by representatives of the local overseas Chinese, paraded through the city in single file. Wherever the cars passed, the overseas Chinese cheered thunderously. Their concern for their motherland is so urgent that it is not easy to imagine without experiencing it firsthand.

Singapore is truly a beautiful city. The buildings are very neat, and the roads are so flat and clean that I have never seen them in China. In addition, it is evergreen all year round, without that desolate and bleak scene. When we passed through the botanical garden, the greenery was shaded and the grass was like a carpet, which made people feel lovely.

After a parade of more than an hour, we arrived at the "Great World" amusement park in Singapore around 1 p.m. Overseas Chinese organizations jointly held a welcoming meeting. Overseas Chinese representatives Lin Qingnian and Hu Changyao gave welcoming speeches successively. You Gengsheng replied on behalf of the delegation. Various organizations presented a "Glory Overseas" banner, which was accepted by Shen Siliang. After the ceremony, a public banquet was held, with Chinese food served. Everyone was tired of eating Western food on the ship, so they changed their tastes at this time and had a full meal.

After the public banquet, the overseas Chinese basketball team will hold a friendly match with the delegation. This letter is waiting to be sent. All the details will be reported after arriving in Colombo. (Sent from Singapore on July 2) (End)

British Selection of World Games Athletes 168

London, 10th (Reuters) The British Amateur Athletics Championships, which select athletes for the World Games, opened today at the White City Stadium. The results are as follows:

Cooper (Great Britain) won the two miles in 13 minutes 50 seconds, beating Radvia Whitehart (also Great Britain) by 60 yards. (Great Britain) came in second.

In the one-mile preliminary, Stokeshart, a promising British half-mile record holder and British, was eliminated. Wutson (Great Britain) and Lerwulock (New Zealand star) qualified for the final.

In the six-mile race, Poland's Nuojie broke the British record of 30 minutes 23.2 seconds with a time of 29 minutes 43.3 seconds, beating second-place De (Great Britain) by five yards. Eden (Great Britain) came in third.

In the triple jump, Australia's Mortoga broke the British record of 46 feet 9 inches with a jump of 49 feet 5 and a half inches. Dickinson (Australia) came in first with 47 feet 11 and three-quarters inches. Bausai (Ireland) came in third with 45 feet 1 inch.

The First Annual Meeting of the China Health Education Society 171

Two General Assemblies Held Yesterday

More Than One Hundred Proposals Passed in Five Groups

Chen Guofu et al. Elected as Directors for This Term

The General Assembly Will Hold a Closing Ceremony This Morning

(Special Dispatch from Zhenjiang) The first annual meeting of the China Health Education Society was held at 8 a.m. yesterday. One hundred and ten members attended the first general assembly, chaired by Xu Shaodi. More than one hundred proposals in five groups were passed. The Education Department hosted a public banquet at noon. The second general assembly was held at 2 p.m., with 104 members attending, chaired by Ye Suzhong. The constitution was revised, temporary proposals were passed, papers were read, and elections began. As a result, Chen Guofu, Zhou Fohei, Hu Dingan, Ye Suzhong, Lei Zhen, Pan Gongzhan, Xu Shaodi, Shao Xiangyin, Cao Chu, Zhu Jiqing, Gao Meifang, Meng Pu, Ma Ketan, Wu Nanxuan, and Yu Hongsheng were elected as directors. Tan Shouren, Yi Junzuo, Chen Bangxian, Tong Zhiqing, and Zai Yuanchen were elected as alternate directors. Niu Yongjian, Wang Qizhang, Weng Zilong, Hu Shuyi, Hu Yiming, Yu Shaolin, and Cheng Gongbao were elected as supervisors. Chen Lifu, Li Ziheng, and Xue Deyi were elected as alternate supervisors.

At 7 p.m., all members attended a banquet hosted by the provincial health and education agencies. The meeting will continue this morning with a closing ceremony. In the afternoon, members will be invited to tour scenic spots. The proceedings of yesterday's meeting are recorded below.

Discussion of Proposals

Health Education Administration Group 1. A proposal from the Society to request the national health education administration authorities to order all provinces, cities, and counties to determine the appropriation of health education funds in the budget to facilitate promotion. (Resolution) Approved in principle, to be submitted to the next board of directors to formulate a plan and submit it to the central government for approval. 2. A proposal from the Society to draft a minimum amount of health education funds for primary schools and submit it to the Ministry of Education for adoption and implementation. (Resolution) To be handled jointly with the previous proposal by the next board of directors. 3. Health education should be added to all levels of normal schools to cultivate general teachers with the ability to promote health education. 4. A proposal to request the government to order all post-secondary normal schools nationwide to add courses on medical common sense. 5. Teacher training should be cultivated for the implementation of health education in primary schools. 6. A proposal from the Society to request the Ministry of Education to stipulate the addition of health and medical knowledge courses in the health departments of normal schools, as well as practice in vaccination and preventive injections, and to order education bureaus in all provinces, cities, and counties to hold vaccination and injection training classes for primary and secondary school teachers. 7. Normal schools should add health and medical common sense courses from the 25th academic year. (Resolution) The above five proposals are merged for discussion and submitted to the next board of directors to designate members to conduct thorough research and submit improvement measures and the number of teaching hours and curriculum standards for health departments at all levels of normal schools, as well as a concrete plan for training primary school teachers to supplement health education at all levels of normal schools, to the Ministry of Education for adoption and implementation. In addition, please ask the Ministry of Education to select universities, education colleges, or medical colleges in China to add health education departments to train health education talents. Female students in secondary schools should pay attention to infant care common sense. (Resolution) Approved in principle, to be submitted to the next board of directors for supplementation and submission to the Ministry of Education for approval. 9. How should the current health textbooks used in primary schools be studied separately to determine selection standards? (Resolution) To be used as a reference by the next board of directors when studying primary school health education materials. 10. How should health facilities in schools be increased? 11. How should the implementation of environmental health in primary schools be promoted? 12. Please ask the Ministry of Education to instruct education departments and bureaus across the country to order primary schools to organize desks and chairs to suit children's homework at all levels, and to ban blackboards from being too dark to avoid harming children's eyesight and to emphasize hygiene. 13. The environmental health of rural primary schools is the worst. How should it be improved? Please discuss. 14. The Society should request the Ministry of Education to order all schools nationwide to ban the use of dry cloths to wipe blackboards and instead use damp cloths, towels, or sponges. 15. Please ask the Society to request the provincial education departments to order county education bureaus (departments) to instruct all levels of schools in the county to build healthy school environments to cultivate students' hygiene habits, and to instill hygiene knowledge in students in a lively way, as a basis for promoting health education. 16. It is proposed to stipulate the lowest standards for school environmental health facilities. (Resolution) The above seven proposals are merged for discussion. Except for the 16th proposal, which has already been stipulated by the central government and does not need to be discussed, the rest are submitted to the next board of directors for detailed supplementation and reorganization to submit improvement opinions and measures to the Ministry of Education for adoption and implementation. 17. It is recommended that the Ministry of Education issue the lowest standards for the implementation of health in rural and urban primary schools and the equipment to be followed by all provinces and counties. 18. The Society should draft the lowest implementation plan for primary school health education (divided into complete primary schools and junior primary schools) and submit it to the Ministry of Education for adoption and implementation in all provinces and cities. (Resolution) The above two proposals are merged for discussion and submitted to the next board of directors for handling. 19. The Society should request the Ministry of Interior to order all provinces, cities, and counties to hold simple vocational health training classes. (Resolution) Approved in principle, to be handled by the next board of directors, with the addition of the public education organization item to the relevant agencies to facilitate implementation.

Public Health Education 1. Establish a rural health care system. (Resolution) Approved in principle, to be handled by the next board of directors. 2. Request the government to designate the Dragon Boat Festival as the Chinese Public Health Festival. (Resolution) Approved in principle, to be handled by the next board of directors. 3. Please suggest that the central government instruct all provincial and municipal governments to build low-income housing and run low-income schools as soon as possible to emphasize low-income public health education. (Resolution) Passed, to be handled by the next board of directors. 4. Raise the authority of midwives to meet social needs. 5. Please earnestly promote scientific delivery methods to help promote health education. (Resolution) The above two proposals are merged and submitted to the next board of directors for supplementation and reorganization, to be suggested to the central government. 6. Please suggest that the central government implement health education for prostitutes and improve the treatment of prostitutes to emphasize national health. (Resolution) To be submitted to the next board of directors to suggest to the central government. 7. The Society should draft measures for local private and public medical institutions to assist in health education in their respective areas, and submit them to the Ministry of Education to be submitted to the Executive Yuan for implementation. Resolution: To be handled by the next board of directors after deliberation.

Youth Health Group 1. Physical examinations should be conducted before and after student sports. (Resolution) To be used by the next board of directors for school health review. 2. Strictly examine the physical fitness of new students. (Resolution) Approved in principle, to be merged by the next board of directors with other student health plans to build the Ministry of Education. 3. Middle schools are urged to strengthen students' physical fitness. (Resolution) Approved in principle, to be built by the next board of directors by the Ministry of Education. 4. Health education should focus on practical activities and should be considered as a whole with physical education, integrating families, schools, and society to maximize the functions of "physical education." 5. School health should be done in cooperation with families. The above two proposals are merged for discussion and submitted to the next board of directors with other school health programs to be suggested to the Ministry of Education.

Children's Health Group 1. Please promote the abolition of the use of waistbands for children. 2. It is proposed to suggest that the authorities order the organization of hygiene teams in primary schools everywhere as the center for the implementation of hygiene education in the 25th academic year. 3. Schools should hire school doctors to be responsible for the health checkups and treatment of diseases of students, and to serve as school health consultants. The above three proposals are merged for discussion. (Resolution) To be submitted to the next board of directors along with the other school health facilities proposals to be suggested to the central government. 4. Please ask the Society to elaborate on the implementation plan for children's mental health in schools and submit it to the Ministry of Education to order all primary schools nationwide to increase children's happiness. 5. Primary school education must focus on the mental health of children. 6. All registered physicians should be ordered by the central competent authority to serve in primary schools in the locality where they practice. 7. Physical education in primary schools should pay special attention to group exercises. All intense sports that are not suitable for children's physical and mental health should be prohibited, and should be implemented separately for boys and girls to suit their needs. The above four proposals are merged for discussion. (Resolution) Approved in principle, to be suggested to the central government by the next board of directors. 8. Control children's reading materials to benefit children's physical and mental health. (Resolution) Passed and submitted to the next board of directors to suggest to the Ministry of Education. 9. The participation of primary school students in fly-catching campaigns should be strictly regulated to emphasize the principles of epidemic prevention. 10. At present, rural primary schools should step up their attention to children's health training. 11. To enable health education to be transmitted from schools to all schools in society, children's family hygiene patrol and inspection teams can be organized. The above three proposals are merged. (Resolution) Approved in principle, to be organized and suggested to the Ministry of Education by the next board of directors. 12. The Society should designate members to study the education methods for children with disabilities. 13. The Society plans to jointly organize a summer health camp for children with the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education next year. The two proposals are merged. (Resolution) To be handled by the next board of directors as appropriate. 14. It is proposed to set up open-air schools for children with latent tuberculosis for remedy. 15. Children with severe malnutrition and amblyopia cannot bear the burden of today's heavy academic subjects. It is proposed to designate schools to add special classes or extend the teaching years. The two proposals are merged. (Resolution) To be studied by the next board of directors. 16. Rural children often suffer from malnutrition, which hinders physical education. How should we try to remedy this? (Resolution) To be studied by the research group.

The Ministry of Education Establishes a Committee to Compile Textbooks for Primary and Secondary Schools 173

Complete the Popular Textbook Part in Half a Year

(Nanjing, 11th) The Ministry of Education has established a Textbook Editing Committee to facilitate the compilation and printing of textbooks for primary and secondary schools and popular education. In addition to Xin Shuzhi, the director of the Compilation and Translation Hall, serving as a permanent member, Yang Zhensheng, Gu Shusen, Lei Zhen, and Chen Lijiang have also been appointed as members, with Yang Zhensheng serving as the chairman. It is reported that the committee has been established and has drafted a work plan outline, which has been submitted to Minister Wang for approval. The committee will complete the popular education textbook part in half a year, the primary school textbook part in one year, and the Chinese, history, and geography parts for middle schools in four years.

City Education Bureau Suppresses Unscrupulous Private Schools' Indiscriminate Enrollment of Students 174

Deliberating Three Measures and Ordering All Schools to Comply

Private schools in this city are numerous, and some regard schools as profit-making institutions, using various improper methods to attract students, even colluding with teachers in neighboring schools to entice large numbers of students to transfer. A group of unscrupulous teachers then use attracting students as a rare commodity to be hoarded and sold, seeing it as a stepping stone for advancement. Such schools and such teachers have a significant impact on the entire education system of this city. It is heard that the City Education Bureau has strictly formulated measures to suppress this: All schools must not use improper methods to attract students. If any incident of utilizing teachers from neighboring schools to entice students to transfer occurs, it will be investigated and dealt with severely without leniency. Teachers who are under contract must not transfer to other teaching positions without the permission of the original headmaster. If any unscrupulous teacher incites students to transfer schools arbitrarily, once evidence is verified, those who are registered will have their registration revoked, and schools must not employ those who are not registered. Schools that employ such unscrupulous teachers will be subject to severe punishment. All schools are hereby ordered to comply.

Regulations for Evaluation and Appointment of Educational Personnel 175

Drafted by the Ministry of Personnel

(Nanjing, 11th) The Ministry of Personnel has drafted an outline for the regulations regarding the evaluation and appointment of educational personnel. Principals of public secondary schools and above, presidents of independent colleges, and heads of public and private social education institutions, after passing review, will be appointed to positions with simplified, recommended, or commissioned ranks. Teachers and staff, after passing review, will receive simplified, recommended, or commissioned rank treatment. Currently, discussions are being held with the Ministry of Education to draft detailed regulations, which will be implemented soon. The evaluation and appointment of educational personnel in private secondary schools and above, as well as public and private elementary schools, will be handled later.

Ministry of Education Issues Order Regarding Practical Issues in Elementary Schools 176

Lower Grade Students Should Have Sufficient Sleep

The Ministry of Education issued a circular to the Education Bureaus of all provinces and cities on the 10th, stating: "According to the report submitted by the National Children's Year Implementation Committee, this committee, in order to pay attention to the health and safety issues of elementary school children, has raised five practical issues in children's education at the 13th committee meeting: Children should have adequate sleep, going to bed from 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM and getting up around 7:00 AM the next morning. It is advisable for lower grade children to have a half-hour nap in the afternoon. The morning class time for elementary schools should not be too early, and the rest time after lunch should not be too short. Parents should be informed to supervise children to go to bed early every night. If lower grade children fall asleep during class due to fatigue, they should be immediately allowed to sleep in a suitable place or simply allowed to do so without prohibition. During the half-hour before morning class and the rest or exercise time after class, there must be at least one teacher on the playground responsible for supervision, maintaining order, protecting children's safety, and guiding games and exercises. Strictly prohibit vendors selling snacks near schools and prohibit children from buying snacks. All elementary schools should pay close attention to the cleanliness of children's drinking water and toilets. It was resolved to 'request the Ministry of Education to order all elementary schools nationwide to pay attention to this matter,' as recorded in the minutes. It is appropriate to record this case and submit a document to your office for review and approval, and request you to order the Education Bureaus of all provinces and cities to instruct all elementary schools under their jurisdiction to strictly comply.'" Based on this, the five practical issues raised by the committee regarding children's education are very important for children's health and safety. In terms of the actual situation of general elementary schools, all the issues raised by the committee should be paid attention to. It is appropriate to order you to be informed and to order all elementary schools under your jurisdiction to strictly comply with this order.
