Cultural Construction Monthly 180

Volume 2, Issue 10 Published

Cultural Construction Monthly, Volume 2, Issue 10, focuses on the discussion of economic and financial issues during extraordinary times. Important articles include Qi Qisheng's "The Farmers Bank and Rural Finance in China", Liu Shiren's "Public Debt Policy During Extraordinary Times", Zhuang Xinzai's "The Issue of Implementing Income Tax in China", and Ka Jintao's "The Issue of Grain Control in China". Economic policies during extraordinary times mainly consist of increasing taxes and issuing public debt. However, in our country, which lacks resources, both of these policies have problems. If you want to know how to remedy this, you must read this issue of Cultural Construction. In addition, there is also Sa Mengwu's "The Problem of China's Local System and Unification", which discusses the necessary conditions for unification based on China's local system since the Zhou and Qin dynasties, and the insights are unique and can be considered a famous work. It is heard that issue 11 of the journal, because the publication date coincides with the 22nd anniversary of the outbreak of World War I in August, the content will focus on the analysis of the current world crisis and the preparations for war by the great powers. It is also heard that the China-Based Cultural Construction Essay Contest, sponsored by the Cultural Construction Association, has been reviewed and the names of the selected people will be announced in that issue. At the same time, one or two of the best micro-articles will be selected for publication for public viewing.

Commercial News

Cotton Yarn Prices Soar Unceasingly; High Cotton Yarn Prices Seen Repeatedly 182

Yarn – 3.5 Yuan Higher Than the Highest Price Last Year; Cotton – Current Month's Chen Cotton Priced at 50 Yuan Less 1 Jiao

Rising Sharply, Falling Quickly

The yarn market rose in the morning and retreated in the afternoon. The highest peak for far-term yarn reached 219.8 yuan, exceeding the highest price of 216.3 yuan on December 4th of last year by 3.5 yuan. This was because American cotton continued to rise, and the new bulls took advantage of the momentum to advance fiercely, so the market price rose steadily. However, due to the high prices, retail investors took profits and sold, and although the bulls tried hard to pull up the market, the market price was inevitably affected by this.

The Rising Trend Only Stopped at Closing

The opening of standard yarn in the morning carried on the remaining power of yesterday's surge, coupled with the continued increase in American cotton. The bulls were elated, and the market price went straight ahead. The current month soared by 4.3 yuan, and the remaining months rose by 2.1 yuan to 3.1 yuan. The second session was firm, rising to 8 jiao. The third session rose by 7 jiao to 1 yuan due to the soaring price of raw cotton. The closing price for July to September was still firm. Unexpectedly, when it came to the October contract, scattered bulls took profits, and there was a lack of buyers for a while, and the market suddenly loosened, falling by 1.4 yuan. The November and December contracts fell by 2 yuan due to the virtual market sentiment in October and the rising selling trend taking advantage of the opportunity. As a result, the near-term price rose by 4.3 yuan to 4.5 yuan compared to yesterday's closing price, and the medium- and long-term prices rose by 1.6 yuan to 3 yuan. The second session opened firm in the afternoon, and after the third session, the price retreated by 1 yuan due to more bulls taking profits. As a result, the price rose by 1.4 yuan to 2.5 yuan compared to yesterday's closing price. According to the investigation, the sellers included: Chengji 1,050 bales, Yukang 1,050 bales, Hengyi 3,500 bales, Yuda 2,515 bales, Jinchang 2,050 bales, Mingde 2,100 bales, Shenchang 2,400 bales, Shenji 1,050 bales, Dachangcheng 1,500 bales, Changfeng 2,450 bales, Dachang 2,900 bales, and Yongdashun 2,400 bales. The buyers included: Deda 1,150 bales, Dafu 2,150 bales, Zhenda 1,450 bales, Hexing 3,900 bales, Yikang 1,000 bales, Shenji 4,350 bales, Taichang 1,700 bales, Jinghua 1,400 bales, Dachang 2,150 bales, and Tonghe 5,000 bales.

Yarn Threads Also Rose by 3-5 Yuan

The sales of spot yarn are still good. The buyers from Xuzhou and other inland areas are more active. A total of 639 bales were traded. The market price rose by 3 yuan for yarn and 5 yuan for thread in the morning, and retreated by about 1 yuan in the afternoon. The purchase amounts of various areas are as follows:

The cotton market rose more sharply due to the continued increase in imported cotton. The price of Chen cotton jumped by 1.85 yuan to 1.95 yuan in the morning, and the price of new cotton rose by 8 jiao. Unexpectedly, the yarn market retreated at the close, and scattered bulls took profits and sought to close their positions, causing a sharp drop of about 1 yuan. In the afternoon, the bulls re-purchased, and the price rose again by 6-7 jiao. However, the market turned loose, and it was not easy to advance, resulting in a rapid rise and fall of the market price. The difference between the various sessions was very large. The market situation was full of ups and downs, which was shocking.

Inevitably Affected by Foreign Cotton

The opening of futures cotton in the morning was due to the continued rise in American cotton, which rose by another 24 to 37 points. Indian cotton also followed suit, continuing to rise. In the second session, Chen cotton jumped again by 6.5 to 7 jiao, and new cotton rose by 2 to 4.5 jiao. In the third session, it rose again by 1 to 5 jiao, rising step by step, and the atmosphere was firm. Unexpectedly, the cotton yarn market suddenly fell at the close, and general scattered bulls closed their positions one after another. The August contract fell sharply by 9 jiao, the September contract fell sharply by 1 yuan, and the October contract for new cotton fell even more sharply, falling by 1.1 yuan in one session. As a result, Chen cotton rose by 9.5 jiao compared to yesterday's closing, while new cotton for October fell by 3 jiao, and the remaining months rose by 1.5 to 2.5 jiao. After the opening in the afternoon, the bulls resumed pulling, and Chen cotton rebounded by 4.5 to 9.5 jiao, and new cotton also rebounded by 3.5 to 8 jiao. After the second session, the market was slightly softer due to frequent closing of positions by scattered bulls, but the trend of Chen cotton was still firm. The closing price was firm. The Yarn Exchange Adds a Special Deposit

The Yarn and Cloth Exchange announced on July 11 that from today onwards, a special deposit of 8 yuan per bale will be collected from both parties for new cotton yarn transactions, and a special deposit of 3 yuan per dan will be collected from both parties for new cotton transactions. The collection of both deposits will be based on one party. In addition, for the new cotton transaction in this month, a special deposit of 3 yuan per dan (totaling 6 yuan) will still be collected according to the same example, and the two deposits will be collected by one party.

Shen Bao Children's Special

On Diligence 197

— Zhang Yizhi

Diligence is the most precious treasure of life and an essential principle for establishing oneself. As the ancient saying goes, "A rope saw can cut through wood, and water droplets can pierce through stone." This is clear evidence of diligence!

There was a villager whose family was very poor, but he was very diligent and hardworking. Even in the scorching summer, when the hot sun made his skin feel like it was about to crack, he still worked diligently without stopping. In the bitterly cold winter, which everyone feared, he was not afraid of the severe cold and worked diligently as usual. After a long time, he gradually became moderately well-off, and later, he gradually became wealthy.

There was also a student who was very slow-witted. He always lagged behind in exams. Later, he felt ashamed and began to study diligently, day and night, regardless of the cold or heat. Over time, his knowledge made great progress. Later, even those who were more gifted than him could not catch up. Children, as long as one is "diligent," the poor can become rich, and the dull can become intelligent. Think about it! How great is the power of diligence!

Now is the age of scientific warfare, children! We should be even more diligent in using our hands and brains. You must know that only science can win and survive in the modern world, and science can only be developed by diligently using our hands and brains.

The Story of Punctuality 198

— Shijiu

The Chinese have never paid much attention to punctuality. For example, when friends meet, they should arrive on time once the time has been set, so as not to break their promise. However, some are late, and some don't show up at all. I think children have personally encountered this kind of thing or heard others talk about it. There are also things like attending meetings and banquets. There are certainly some who can be punctual, but there are also many who are not. I won't say much more about that here. Now, let me tell you a story about someone who was criticized for being punctual, and as a result, the person who was late was the one who was embarrassed:

During the Later Han Dynasty, there was a man named Chen Shi, who was also known as Zhonggong. His virtue was admired by everyone. After he died, more than 30,000 people from all over the country came to mourn him, and more than 100 people wore mourning clothes. He had two sons: one named Ji, also known as Yuanfang, and one named Chen, also known as Jifang. Because they received a good family education from an early age, Yuanfang and Jifang were also very famous. Chen's family history has been briefly described. Next, I will talk about Mr. Zhonggong's story of punctuality.

One day, Mr. Zhonggong and a friend agreed to go to a place together, and the agreed time was noon. However, when noon arrived, the friend had not yet arrived, so Mr. Zhonggong went alone. After he left, the friend arrived. When he arrived in front of Chen's house, he saw Yuanfang playing. At that time, he was only seven years old. He asked, "Is your father at home?" Yuanfang replied, "It has been a long time since I saw you, and my father has already left." The visitor heard this and angrily said, "He's not human! He made an appointment with me and left by himself." Yuanfang said, "You and my father agreed to meet at noon. If you don't arrive at noon, you are untrustworthy, and it is rude to scold his father in front of someone else's son!" The friend's face turned red after being told by Yuanfang. He hurriedly got out of the car and wanted to hug Yuanfang, but Yuanfang ran into the house and ignored him.

Children! Mr. Zhonggong did nothing wrong. His friend broke his promise, but instead wanted to call him "inhuman," so it is no wonder that he was embarrassed. Yuanfang was only seven years old at the time, but he already knew etiquette, which is also admirable. From this story, it can be seen that the habit of being unpunctual has been around since ancient times, and we should correct it ourselves.

Photography 199

— Zhen

Min'er is a sixth-grade student in elementary school, and he has already graduated this year. Before graduating, the students felt that they would be separated from now on, so their feelings were very harmonious. They exchanged their own photos to keep as a permanent memento. Of course, Min'er also had many classmates who asked him for photos, so he decided to go to the photo studio on Sunday to take pictures. In less than a week, the photos were printed. When he went to the photo studio to pick up the photos, he had a big question:

"Sir, how can you put my image on this paper in a few seconds?"

"It would take a long explanation to answer that question. I have to tell you from beginning to end: The most important thing in photography is the film. Use a glass plate or a kind of soft paper, and coat one side with a kind of chemical medicine and let it dry. That is the film. What is the use of this film? Put the film in the camera box, and the thing you want to photograph will be directly shot onto the film through the lens. The chemical medicine on the film will change when it sees light. Moreover, the light is strong or weak, then the changes on the film will also be deep or shallow. But the changes are very small, so the image on the film cannot be seen. So you have to find a way to make it clear. Development: After the chemical medicine on the film is acted upon by the developer, all the places that have been exposed to light will change into a black thin layer and attach to the film. The stronger the light, the faster the decomposition, and the darker the color. Therefore, the brightest part of the scene is the darkest on the film, which is exactly the opposite of the correct image, so the image on the film is called the negative image. After the negative image is printed, there will inevitably be many unchanged chemical medicines on the film, so it cannot be exposed to light, because if the unchanged medicine encounters light, it will change again, and won't it ruin the film? So it must go through a fixing procedure. Immerse the film in a fixing medicine to fix the image, and then wash it with water to completely wash away the medicine on the film, and the changed medicine will still remain on the film. This is the black negative in your hand. To make the image into a photograph, you need a special paper. This special paper is made in the same way as the film. Put the negative on the paper and expose it to sunlight. The light-transmitting parts of the negative will change the medicine on the paper, and the non-transmitting parts will not change the medicine. In this way, the image on the paper will be exactly in line with the original scene. After such a complicated procedure, it can become a photograph."

Lilliput 200

— Zhu Chengxi

Lilliput, so small, let me slowly tell you the wonders. Don't quarrel, don't make noise, I guarantee you'll laugh when you hear it!

Peanut shells are used as boats, and match sticks are good for punting. Tipping over a teacup becomes a flood, and the men and women cry and wail. Mother cuts clothes and the scraps of cloth that fall are less than three inches. The little people carry them to make clothes, three hundred sets in all sizes.

Three grains of rice are considered few, but the little people steal them to use as bread. They ate them for three years and six months, and two grains are still left.

The Lilliputian king inspects the troops, and arrays of airplanes and cannons. The cannons are like copper pen caps, and the airplanes are even smaller than dragonflies.

Lilliput is so wonderful, this world can't find it. If you want to visit Lilliput, dream a dream and go to sleep.

Fruit Hygiene 201

— Ziying

Children: As soon as summer comes, many fruits are on the market: peaches, plums, waxberries, watermelons...

Many people teach us to eat more vegetables and fruits. Yes, fruits are not only delicious, but also rich in nutrients, which are very beneficial to our bodies. However, sometimes if you are not careful, they can be harmful. So we must pay attention to the following points:

First, do not eat on the road, because the roads are dusty and contain many germs, which is very unhygienic to eat; and there are many pedestrians, so how difficult is it to eat while running?

Second, the fruits sold by vendors on the roadside are inevitably attached to flies, so we should wash them with clean water at home before eating them. If you want to peel or cut them open, you must first pay attention to whether the knife used is clean.

Third, although fruits are good for the body, it is also unhygienic to eat too much. It is best to eat a little after meals.

Other things like: you must wash your hands before eating; rotten and unripe fruits should not be eaten; ...are hygienic.

The Eight Principles of the Character "Yong" 202

— Chengming

Children! In addition to reading, you also have a writing course, which is also very important, because as your knowledge gradually progresses, your calligraphy must also be gradually practiced to be elegant and beautiful, so that the articles you write are clear and your calligraphy is excellent. But there are many principles for writing! I will now talk about the "Eight Principles of the Character 'Yong'!"

During the Tang Dynasty, there was a great calligrapher named Zhang Huaiwan. He had a lot of research on calligraphy. He once used the character "Yong" as a ratio, calling it the Eight Principles of the Character "Yong". First is "Ce", which is also a point, meaning that a point should be slanted and not straight. Second is "Le", which is a horizontal stroke, meaning that a horizontal stroke should be restrained and have a pause, which is what the common saying calls "soft and hard". Third is "Nu", which is a straight stroke, and a straight stroke is "vertical", meaning that it must be done with force. Fourth is "", "pronounced ti", which is a hook, meaning that a hook is like a hook. Fifth is "Ce", which is a diagonal stroke upwards, which means brevity. Sixth is "Lüe", which is a downward-sloping stroke, and a long downward-sloping stroke is called Lüe, which is like a snatch, meaning agility. Seventh is "Zhuo", which is a short downward-sloping stroke on the right side, and a short downward-sloping stroke is called Zhuo, which is like a quick advance. Eighth is "Zhe", "pronounced zhai", which is a press, and the lower right side of calligraphy is called Zhe, meaning a slow movement. The Eight Principles of the Character "Yong" diagram is published below. "Some say that the Eight Principles of the Character 'Yong' was created by Wang Xizhi."

The Smallest Country in the World 203

— Shun

—and the Country with the Smallest Population

Children, perhaps you already know that the largest countries in the world are the United Kingdom (including its territories), Soviet Russia, the Republic of China...; the countries with the largest populations are also these countries. However, I dare to say boldly that you may not have noticed the smallest country in the world and the country with the smallest population! Let me tell you here, perhaps you would like to know!

The smallest country in the world is Monaco, which is known as the gambling country. It is in the southeast corner of France, facing the Mediterranean Sea. Its area is only eight square miles, and its population is only a few tens of thousands of people. Its political system is a constitutional monarchy. There is a national gambling house in the country, and the country's income almost entirely depends on gambling tax.

The country with the smallest population in the world is a small republic in the Pyrenees Mountains in Europe, called Andorra. The population in this country is only more than 5,000 people. The residents are Basque people who live by animal husbandry. It is located between France and Spain and is protected by the Christian priests of the two countries. Because the territory is all rugged mountains, transportation is inconvenient, and the customs still have a generational flavor.

Scientific Problems

How Does Fanning Make Us Cool? 205

— Zixi

In hot weather, everyone invariably picks up a fan and starts fanning, bringing a refreshing breeze that makes us feel cool and comfortable all over. How does fanning drive away heat and create coolness? This is truly a scientific question that needs to be understood urgently. Now, let me explain it in detail: When the weather is hot, we always sweat profusely. Naturally, most of the sweat is water, which evaporates into vapor and dissipates. However, when water turns into vapor, it absorbs a large amount of heat. Our body heat is lost due to the evaporation of sweat.

However, the speed of sweat evaporation varies with the humidity of the air. In other words, if the air contains less water vapor, the sweat evaporates quickly; if the air contains more water vapor, the sweat evaporates slowly. When we sweat, the amount of water vapor in the air around our body gradually increases, and the evaporation process gradually slows down. Our body heat cannot be dissipated quickly, so we still feel very hot. Conversely, if we fan a few times, making the air circulate, the air near us containing more water vapor flows away, and the air farther away containing less water vapor also flows closer to us. The air around the human body contains only a small amount of water vapor, and sweat evaporates naturally quickly. Our body heat can also be dissipated quickly. At this time, we will naturally feel cooler.

Summer Work 206

— Liu Zhutong, Age 12

Mini Speech

We Must Learn from the Great Hua Mulan 207

— Shen Jifen, Zhujiege Elementary School

Speaking of Hua Mulan, you all know that she was a brave girl, right? But in China's long history, she can also be said to be a great national hero.

Hua Mulan lived during the Sui Dynasty. She had a father, a mother, an older sister, and a younger brother. Her father was a military general at home. At that time, she lived a life of weaving, which was very happy.

At that time, there was a foreign tribe on the northwest border who wanted to seize our complete territory, so the country greatly mobilized its troops, preparing to resist those strong and savage foreigners. The conscription notice also had Mulan's father's name, which made Mulan anxious for many days, because her father was already old and could no longer go out to fight the enemy. She had no older brother to replace her father at the front line. What could she do? She said to herself, "Just because I am a woman, can't I win glory for the country? Can't I replace my aging father in battle? No! I must go. For my father, for my country, I must try. But what I hate the most is this unenlightened society, which fundamentally does not allow women to go to the front line. If I wear men's clothes, wouldn't I look like a man?" As a result, she got her parents' consent, disguised herself as a man, and went on an expedition alone. Later, she fought the enemy, traversed thousands of mountains and rivers, and killed many enemy soldiers and generals. Ah! Mulan was extremely brave! She said, "I will resist to the end! I must kill all those enemy bandits." Sure enough, because she was bold and careful, she truly defeated the enemy soldiers, causing them to flee in disarray. Mulan won the battle against the enemy soldiers, was promoted to general, and led her troops back to the capital. In total, she had been away for twelve years and returned home with the emperor's praise.

Everyone! The story of Mulan? My speech ends here. So let's think about it: If people want to do great things, as long as they have courage and perseverance, they can achieve success. At the same time, whether male or female, they can equally achieve success in great undertakings. Mulan's service in the army in place of her father is a good example.

However, there are still some people who ultimately believe that women's abilities are inferior to men's: what men can do, women cannot do. This is wrong. What men dare to do, women dare not do. That is an even greater mistake. Therefore, teachers often say to us, "Your responsibilities in the future are very heavy!" Yes, in the future, women and men will have equally heavy responsibilities. In the future, when we grow up, we must also learn from Hua Mulan and have the spirit to bravely kill the enemy! Only then will no one dare to bully us.

(Editor's note) The manuscript on the right is the speech of Ms. Shen Yunfen, who has won four consecutive championships in the Qingpu County's elementary school speech contest. Please pay attention, children!

The Tale of a Loyal Dog (26) 208

— Xinqing

Because there had just been a snowfall, Little Nanluo's footprints were indeed very blurred. One could faintly see that he was heading towards Anfan'er Town. Bodexi searched until midnight before entering the dark and narrow streets outside the town. This Anfan'er Town was also completely shrouded in darkness. Occasionally, a sliver of light leaked out from the window panels of people's homes. Sometimes, a group of people would go home with lanterns, already drunk, humming songs in their mouths. The streets were covered with snow, a皑皑 white. The tall, black walls and roofs were set off by the white snow. Everything around was quiet and silent, only the sound of the wind whistling louder and louder, shaking the tall poles of the streetlights.

Because pedestrians often walked past, disturbing the footprints, it was even more difficult for Bodexi to find Little Nanluo. However, it did not retreat and continued to move forward bravely. Although the cold wind was piercing to the bone, the solid ice pricked its feet, and the hunger was burning in its stomach, none of it could dispel its courage. It continued to advance, advance, enduring endless hardships, and finally followed Little Nanluo's footprints up the stone steps of the Great Cathedral.

Bodexi vaguely thought, "He ran off to see his beloved thing again." Although it didn't understand what this was all about, it held full pity and sympathy for Little Nanluo's passion for art.

That night, the Great Cathedral held a midnight mass. One of the doors happened to be left unlocked, perhaps because the worshipers were eager to return home and neglected to lock it. So, Bodexi followed a line of faint footprints and rushed into the door, leaving a lot of white snow on the dark stone floor. It walked all the way to the front of the altar and saw Little Nanluo, whom it had been searching for so desperately, lying stiffly on the stone steps. It quietly crawled forward and touched Little Nanluo's face, as if saying to him, "Did you think I was an unrighteous thing, and sought my own comfort by abandoning you? Did you think I was an ordinary dog?"

Little Nanluo gave a low cry and hugged Bodexi tightly. He whispered to it, "Let us lie down and die together. People do not need us. We are alone in this world." Bodexi crawled closer and pressed its head against Little Nanluo's chest. Its melancholy brown eyes contained two big bubbles of tears, expressing the joy in its heart.

The two of them lay close together in the bone-chilling cold. Gusts of wind swept over the river from the northern ocean, resembling ice waves. Anything that came into contact with them would be frozen. They lay in the middle of this huge stone cellar, which felt even colder than the snow-covered plain outside. A bat often flew in the shadows—a ray of light often shone directly on the rows of statues. Together they lay beneath the icons painted by Robens, motionless, as if they had fallen asleep because they were frozen by the cold. They dreamed of the happy days of the past, when they often chased each other in the meadows full of flowers, or sat together in the reeds by the water, watching the ships sail out to sea in the sunlight.

There was never a dark cloud hovering over the friendship between Little Nanluo and Bodexi, so they always loved and cherished each other and never separated. In their short lives, they had fulfilled their responsibilities and had not wronged anyone. They had never committed any sins in their lives, so they were very happy and satisfied in their conscience. They were attacked by both hunger and cold, and the blood in their veins seemed to be gradually freezing, but they were still dreaming of the happy times of the past, passing the long night.

Shenbao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

Economic Exchange

Reasons for High Prices and Food Shortages in Germany 209

— Yuanting

On September 4th of last year, the German government announced the highest prices for beef, pork, sausage, eggs, and other items, stipulating that the prices of these items should not exceed the levels of March 1935. This clearly shows that because prices in Germany were rising day by day, the Hitler government had no choice but to use orders to suppress them. However, this situation of high prices cannot be seen in the statistics of German officialdom. For example, the statistics of German officialdom in June, July, August, and September of last year are like this:

Such official statistics are based on several commodities with unchanging prices, made according to government regulations. Therefore, the prices of the general market cannot be seen in the middle.

Generally speaking, in the current state of Germany, the real situation of high prices in Germany cannot be seen in general newspapers and magazines either. However, some German publications sometimes reveal a little bit of accurate information in a roundabout way. For example, the magazine "German Economist" stated: "It is obvious that the movement of the food index is mainly determined by commodities with unchanging prices (such as milk, bread, etc.), but the proportion of these items to food transactions is not decisive. Moreover, according to the report of the statistical authorities, the prices of items such as cheese, sausage, vegetable oil, and fruits are far above the statistical figures." If this is translated into very straightforward language, it means that the statistics of German officialdom are based on commodities with unchanging prices, and these commodities have no decisive significance for market transactions, so the statistics of officialdom are tantamount to deception.

In recent years, the price policy of the Hitler government has, on the one hand, prevented the official prices of grain from increasing, but on the other hand, it has made the prices of livestock feed rise day by day. The year before last, because the harvest was not good, grain was less than four million tons, and the increase in imports only supplemented 500,000 tons. This made grain even more scarce, and the price of feed naturally became more expensive in lean years. Feed, needless to say, is produced by the land, so its expensive price is of course beneficial to landowners and wealthy farmers, but on the other hand, it is a major blow to the lives of poor and middle peasants. Because raising livestock is the main sideline business of general farmers, the high price of feed has greatly reduced their income from raising livestock, sometimes even making this income fundamentally problematic. This is of course very distressing for them, who are usually very weak and poor. At the same time, the current policy of the German government also wants to limit the rise in livestock and meat prices. As a result, it is even more unfavorable for farmers who raise livestock.

Because of the high price of feed and the restriction of livestock and meat prices, the number of livestock raised by farmers has decreased accordingly, resulting in a great shortage of meat and oil. Taking pigs as an example, the number of pigs raised by farmers last year decreased by 10% compared to the previous year. The number of pigs used for slaughter also decreased by more than 15.9%. Recently, this decrease is still developing.

The lack of these kinds of goods in Germany can be seen even more in the imports of meat and oil last year and the year before last. Please see the table below——(Unit: 1,000 tons)

What is particularly noteworthy in the middle is the large decrease in oilseeds and other items used as the basis for the production of artificial cheese. Because these contain 35% oil, the reduction in their imports by that much means a reduction in fats and oils of 250,000 tons, which represents a deficiency of one-half of Germany's butter consumption.

But what exactly are the reasons for such high prices and food shortages in Germany? According to the official German explanation, it lies in the improved lives of the German people and the increased needs. An official magazine said: "We feel a slight lack of some agricultural products today. In fact, this lack is a good phenomenon. We must remember that for many important reasons, the demand for production has increased, and consequently, its consumption has also increased. If one examines the fact that 4.5 million people have returned to the production process, resulting in an increase in purchasing power, then this problem can be fully understood. In this case, the increase in purchasing power must first affect the food market." Thus, there is a great shortage of food, and its price is rising day by day. At the same time, the state-run Economic Research Institute followed the instructions of Propaganda Minister Goebbels and said, "In any case, a lack of food has occurred. But this fact is nothing more than an explanation of increased needs. This is also the same for bread and milk for drinks. At the same time, as a result of the increased need for milk for drinks, the amount of milk used by bread manufacturers has decreased. Naturally, the increased needs also include the increased needs of the military, but the main reason is still the increased happiness of the people." This also clearly attributes the reasons for high prices and food shortages in Germany to the increased objective needs and the improved lives of the people.

But in fact, as mentioned above, the lives of general German farmers are becoming increasingly impoverished because of poor harvests, high feed prices, difficulty in making profits from raising livestock, and heavy burdens of various taxes and levies. Their consumption capacity is naturally greatly reduced; the so-called improved lives of the people, increased general consumption capacity, upward purchasing power, etc., are completely the opposite for general German farmers. As for the laborers in the cities, their lives are also becoming increasingly impoverished. Facts tell us that in the year before the crisis began, the total income of German laborers was 44.57 trillion marks. By 1932, their total income was only 26 trillion marks. Comparing the two, it decreased by almost half. As for last year, it is said that the income of German laborers has rebounded to 31.76 trillion marks. But according to Germany's huge budget this year, German laborers will probably have to bear even greater taxes in the future, and their income will probably decrease even more; moreover, the German government's method of reducing unemployment is to exploit employed workers to provide relief to unemployed workers, so in reality, even if the total income of the laborers has increased somewhat, their individual income is decreasing. According to the "German Economist," published in Germany, the reasons hindering the revival of Germany's consumer industry are these two: "First, compared with the period of increased business activity in the past, wages have only increased a little; as a result, the total wage amount has only increased a little even with the increase in the number of employed people. Second, most of this income has flowed into the national treasury in the form of taxes." If this reveals a little bit of accurate information, then it means that the income of German laborers has not actually increased recently. In this way, since the income of urban laborers in Germany has not increased, and is even decreasing, and on the other hand, prices are rising day by day and the standard of living is increasing day by day, then their lives, of course, are becoming increasingly impoverished, just like the farmers in the countryside, and their consumption power is decreasing day by day.

Based on this fact, it can be clearly understood that the reason for the rise in prices in Germany is not the increase in objective needs or the upward purchasing power; on the contrary, it is because the increasing impoverishment of German farmers, workers, and general small citizens hinders the revival and development of the consumer industry, which is why there is a great shortage of general consumer goods and prices are rising day by day. In addition to this, there are two other major reasons: The first is the tendency of currency inflation, which artificially raises general prices; this phenomenon is obviously a major contradiction with the German government's policy of suppressing price increases. The second is Germany's active preparations for war and efforts to expand its military in recent years. This not only requires the storage of large quantities of food, which makes general food increasingly scarce and prices increasingly high; but also, due to the implementation of underground construction projects, airfields, expansion of civil aviation routes, development of various military industries, and compulsory purchase of anti-poison equipment, etc., in the active preparation for war and expansion of military equipment, the general consumer production is decreasing day by day. It can be said that the blood and sweat sucked from the general population is completely used in those non-productive enterprises for preparing for war!

Life

Local Militia 210

— Zhang Zhanyuan

Tianxing Fortress is a high mountain near us, and no such strategically important fortress can be found within a forty-mile radius. I remember my grandfather telling us when we were little that when Lan Dashun rebelled, my grandfather's father and his peers hid in this fortress, thus avoiding disaster. Lan Dashun spent a month trying to capture this mountain fortress, but failed, which shows how dangerous Tianxing Fortress was. Even when we were little, when the "Red Borders" (referring to Yunnan soldiers wearing red-trimmed hats) passed by, this fortress became a place of refuge for nearby residents. Since the Republic's revolution, with wars and chaos, and the countryside being unsettled, this fortress has often been inhabited by wealthy families.

My life as a member of the local militia also began here. Although I have been reorganized into a regular army for two years now, the taste of being a member of the militia a few years ago still often brings back memories. It turns out that life in the militia was much more relaxed, much more enjoyable, and much more interesting than life in the regular army. It was definitely not like now, where I am bound by iron-like discipline and must absolutely obey orders. The situation back then was truly poetic, while now I am truly living a prosaic life.

I also didn't willingly become a member of the militia. In an era of rural bankruptcy and economic depression, there were always many unemployed poor people in the countryside who had nothing to eat. Besides becoming petty thieves, they also formed groups of three or five to commit robberies. The victims were naturally the local "gentry and taxpayers," but the people protecting the peace of the countryside were not the gentry themselves, but the strong young men from ordinary middle-class farming families who were selected and paid for by the gentry and taxpayers. Initially, training was only conducted during the off-season for farming. Every December, the "chief person" in the town would hold the "roster" of each village, selecting one out of every three men, or two out of every five, for training. This was called "door-to-door training," or "household training," which no one could avoid, except for wealthy families who could use money or orders to have their "tenant farmers" take their place. I was a son of a middle-class farming family, about to graduate from elementary school. During the winter vacation, I was inevitably selected for "door-to-door training." At that time, I was also very curious and eager to experience military life. Although household training only required "mustering" (meaning all the strong men gathering in the market town for drills) on days ending in "2, 6, or 9," when people "milling" around at the "temple clearing" in the town center, were "marching" in the group, chanting "One, two, three, four," it always felt like a taste of military life. Early in the morning, the mountain peaks at the edge of the village would echo with the sound of the copper gong. After the gong, you could hear a loud shout: "All registered strong men are hereby notified that the Yongxing Market Township Militia Office orders you to immediately gather under the banyan tree clearing in the street market to await mustering..." Soon, strong men of various colors from each village, carrying guns, wearing short shirts, and straw sandals, would set off from their homes and "rendezvous" at the market town. Our weapons at that time were extremely disorganized. Some carried "bird guns," some wielded spears, some carried iron rods, some carried "torches," and some carried "clappers." As for clothing, it was even more of a motley collection. Some naturally wore military uniforms, these were veterans who had returned home, they always held official positions in the door-to-door training, either as battalion commander, company commander, platoon leader, or at least as a "quartermaster," because they had all received formal military training. In addition, students from middle and high schools who returned home for winter and summer vacations also wore "student uniforms" or "exercise clothes," but the remaining many "ordinary people" had to make do with the blue cloth short shirts they wore for farming. Some people who often ran small businesses were selected, and because they couldn't prepare short shirts, some also rolled up their long gowns and tied them with belts. In short, the door-to-door training was the most diverse team imaginable. Its mission was to listen to the gong, gather in the street market, and wait for "drills," but it had no other use. If bandits really came, they couldn't deal with them, and they would also "turn a blind eye," pretending not to know.

However, when "winter defense" was tight, the door-to-door training, under the order of the "chief commander," had to brave the wind and snow to go out on patrol at night. I remember several years ago, when the situation suddenly became tense, I couldn't even study in my school anymore. During the day, I naturally carried a "rifle" and drilled on the field, and at night, I climbed up the hillside to "stand guard." I wore a "saber" on my waist, carried a gun on my back, and wore thick clothes. Together with three or five other strong men, each patrolled their respective intersections, and everyone knew the password of the team. I also carried "clappers" on my body, and if there was a bandit alarm, I would "whistle" or "shout," or heavily "knock on the clappers." In the woods, under the cliffs, I always had to endure until the rooster crowed before returning home.

Since I couldn't study anymore, and the countryside continued to be unsettled, I officially joined the newly established "militia" from the door-to-door training, also called the local militia, and was stationed at the strategically important Tianxing Fortress. Life in the local militia was much more orderly than in the door-to-door training. Every morning, we would get up at five o'clock, wash up in ten minutes, and gather on the training field in the faint morning light for morning exercises, and have breakfast at six o'clock. The day consisted of "three drills and two lectures," from five o'clock in the morning until nine o'clock in the evening. As for the uniforms worn by the militia, they were naturally much more uniform, and the firearms were also complete. There was also a fixed base, and the training was long-term. Tianxing Fortress was our barracks. There was a temple in the fortress, and each hall was assigned as the captain's office, soldiers' quarters, communication room, bugler's room, cook's room, etc. The captains were naturally soldiers or sergeants and platoon leaders who had retired from the regular army. The soldiers were selected from the door-to-door training. The militia could also receive pay. In addition to donating rice, firewood, and other food supplies every month, the "taxpayers" also contributed some money. Our captain could get three to five silver dollars a month, and we soldiers only got one dollar for pocket money, to be used for buying tobacco and straw sandals. All the firearms were donated by the taxpayers, and very few were purchased by the town government. The guns were mostly homemade breech-loading guns, with names such as "Nine-Shot," "Five-Shot," "Mauser," "Clapboard," and "Single-Needle." "Repeating guns" (i.e., pistols) were only available to the battalion commander.

Although we had three drills and two lectures every day, drilling marching, running, lying down, assembling, and disbanding, life seemed very tense, but in reality, it was very fun. Every Saturday, we could take turns going home. I could be affectionate with my mother, younger brothers, and sisters, whom I hadn't seen for half a month. On Sunday afternoon, I would carry my washed clothes back up the mountain, and occasionally bring some snacks, pickled vegetables, and meat to the fortress to "share" with my brothers. You could also apply for a leave once a month, to freely go to the "market" and freely go "visiting relatives." Every afternoon, after dinner, when it was still early, we would sometimes carry our hands and sing military songs loudly on the training field, such as "A man's first ambition is high, come learn military drills, brother holds the command saber, younger brother fires cannons, the white flag flutters in the wind, the war drums beat..." endlessly. Watching the houses far down the mountain, with wisps of smoke rising from the roofs, hearing us sing military songs, the children in the village would also come out to see, and after a while, they would also learn to sing with us. Sometimes we would also climb to nearby peaks to rest and chat. Looking down at the forests and the golden sunset reflecting on the mountains, watching the shepherds driving cattle and sheep back, we would play until it was dark before returning, and if it wasn't our turn to "be on duty" that night, we could play until late.

But every time the "market" season came, we couldn't avoid forming a team to go down the mountain, go to the market to "muster," walk a few steps in the crowd, pose in a few formations, and then return to the fortress. At night, if it was your turn to "be on duty," it would be a bit painful, especially when the "situation was not good." Every one or two miles, there would be a "sentry post" made of thatched grass on each mountain pass, and strong men would be stationed there every night. The militia would have to "inspect the sentry" every night, to see if there were strong men in the sentry post, and to see if they were fulfilling their duties. Sometimes they would also deliberately attack them to test their alertness. Sometimes, carrying guns, they would patrol in the dark snowy nights. Listening to the whistling of the wind in the mountain forest, the rustling of the snow, everything was silent. At this time, you would feel a little scared and a little lonely. But after passing the password and "meeting the sentry," you could sit on the warm grass pile in the sentry post and rest. There was tobacco, warm tea, and dry pancakes and sorghum wine, which the strong men were waiting for us to take and offer to us. The sentry post was filled with an atmosphere of harmony, a warm smell, not afraid of the fierce wind and snow outside the post.

In addition to our own team going to the market town to "muster," there would also be a "grand parade" every three or four months, probably gathering the militia from the surrounding four or five towns to drill together. We always looked forward to such an opportunity, as it was like taking a trip. During the march, we stepped in orderly steps, singing loud military songs, which echoed back from the mountains. After the parade, we could also receive rewards from the chief commanders or the director of the militia bureau.

The nearby people were either relatives or friends with us, and they were very harmonious with us and not afraid at all. If we occasionally needed some miscellaneous items, such as vegetables or rice straw, we could also send someone to the people at the foot of the mountain to ask for them, and they would all offer them without hesitation. Sometimes, when the situation wasn't tight, and our drills weren't strict, we could take time to go to the people at the foot of the mountain to do "farm work" for them, and they were also very welcome, and they would give us good wine and good food to eat. When it snowed heavily, we would also carry guns, blow "foreign horns," and go on "snow marches" with the children of the people at the foot of the mountain, and sing the "Snow March Song" together: "The mountain bugle blows, the people at the foot of the mountain open their doors. People at the foot of the mountain, don't be alarmed, we are not foreign soldiers, nor are we thieves in the mountains, but we are here to march in the snow, to fight and win for you in the future, and protect our four hundred million Chinese..."

Introduction to "Ice Cream Making Method" 211

As the heat is soaring and the summer heat is oppressive, ice cream is indeed a wonderful product to relieve the heat. Now, the expert Mr. Wu Xinfa has published a book called "Ice Cream Making Method" based on his daily experiences, which describes the procedures for making ice cream in various flavors such as vanilla bean, thick soup, chocolate, walnut, strawberry, lemon, banana, apple, rose, egg, and cream, the preparation of spices and tools, the origin of bacteria, the identification of stale and poisonous changes, and the relationship with personal hygiene. The manufacturing method is simple and easy to understand after reading, which can be said to be self-taught. The whole book has eight chapters and seventy pages thick. The writing is clear and fluent. The actual selling price of each book is two dimes. The stationery departments of Shanghai Life Bookstore, Wing On, Sincere, and The Sun Company all sell them. If you cannot buy them, you can directly send a letter to Shanghai Post Office Box 1737, and we will send them to you immediately.

Scientific Chatter

Solar Eclipse Observation 212

— Jun

The explanation of solar eclipses has always been very mysterious to the general public without knowledge. As soon as they see a solar eclipse occur, they either say that a heavenly dog is eating the sun, or that a demon is swallowing the sun; and immediately, they beat gongs and drums, hoping that the sun will recover, otherwise the human world will be in long-term darkness and there will be no light forever. If you want to say that this is superstition, then they will ask you: Why is it that after people beat gongs and drums and pray during a solar eclipse, the eaten sun quickly recovers? The sun being eaten and recovering due to prayer is clear evidence that the solar eclipse has supernatural effects. This is an absolutely unbreakable truth! Of course, people like these cannot understand the scientific significance of solar eclipses for a while, which requires long-term social education. At the same time, there are also some people who know a little bit about science, who also know a little bit about the astronomical knowledge of solar eclipses, but they do not understand the meaning of actually studying solar eclipses. They often ask such stupid questions: What is the relationship between solar eclipses and human life? What is the practical benefit of studying solar eclipses? This can be said to be completely a merchant-like calculation, thinking that scientific research is only beneficial and meaningful if it studies opening gold mines or invents things that can be sold for a lot of money, and that the study of solar eclipses cannot make a profit, so it is of course not related to human life and is useless. This kind of expression is really snobbish!

However, the actual study of solar eclipses can not only break general superstitions, but also has great significance for astronomy and even general science. For example, the observation of the solar eclipse in South America and other places on May 29, 1919, confirmed the Einstein effect, making his theory of relativity even more radiant, which is deeply related to general science and even world thought. Because the study of solar eclipses is so important, when a total eclipse occurs somewhere, astronomers and scientists from all over the world will travel to observe it, regardless of the hard work; if it is said that the study of solar eclipses is meaningless, then what are the scientists who observe solar eclipses for?

Partial solar eclipses occur three or four times a year, but total eclipses occur only every few years, and can only be seen in certain parts of the earth. Therefore, observing total eclipses is quite difficult; many famous scientists in the world believe that total eclipses are rare research opportunities, so whenever a total eclipse is about to be seen somewhere, they will spare no expense in money and energy, and go in organized and planned teams to observe it. The most recent total eclipse was observed in Siberia in the Soviet Union and Hokkaido in Japan, and more scientists went to study it than before. For a time, the so-called observation of solar eclipses became a major cultural news in the world.

According to past research, the so-called solar eclipse occurs when the moon moves between the earth and the sun, and sunlight is blocked by the moon; a total eclipse is the phenomenon in which the moon completely blocks sunlight in certain areas of the earth. This is already an undoubted truth. The current study of solar eclipses is of course not just to further prove this truth, but has new purposes and meanings. For example, the purpose of the recent solar eclipse research can probably be listed as these points:

First, study the solar atmosphere. The sun that we usually see with the naked eye is a large luminous sphere with a diameter of 1.4 million kilometers. Around this is the solar atmosphere; around this solar atmosphere, there is an even thinner gas body called the corona. Because the sunlight is very strong, we cannot usually observe this corona; only during a total eclipse is there a good opportunity to observe it.

Second, observe how Einstein's proposed light refraction actually occurs in the atmosphere?

Third, observe the relative movement of the sun and the moon to predict the future movement of the moon.

In addition, there are purposes for non-astronomers to observe total eclipses, which are to investigate: 1. the relationship between solar eclipses and cosmic rays; 2. how solar eclipses affect climate; ... and so on.

This solar eclipse started in the Mediterranean Sea, crossed Siberia, proceeded along the northeast coast of Hokkaido, and ended in the Pacific Ocean. The total eclipse time in Siberia was two and a half minutes, and in Hokkaido it was one minute and fifty seconds, so observation was quite difficult. However, due to modern observation equipment, the observation results have obtained many valuable materials; after these materials have been sorted and studied for a long time, they will be published and will correctly answer the above-mentioned questions, thus having a significant impact on science and world thought. In this way, who can still say that this is useless compared to past general solar eclipse research?

Travels Around the World

Mount Emei 213

—

The Jiangnan region has very few mountains; as far as the eye can see, there are endless open fields. People who grow up in these fields, apart from visiting Mount Hui in Wuxi and Tianzhu in Hangzhou, can only appreciate the charm of mountains through books and paintings. However, if you enter Sichuan, you are guaranteed to encounter mountains similar to Mount Hui and Tianzhu everywhere. Just sitting on the bow of a boat and looking at the majestic cliffs on both sides of the Wu Gorge is enough for you to savor, let alone disembarking and continuing west?

The ancients said, "The Jian'ge Pass is the most dangerous place in the world, and Mount Emei is the most beautiful." We will not concern ourselves with how dangerous the Jian'ge Pass is for the time being; we will now look at how beautiful Mount Emei is.

To climb Mount Emei, you must first take a boat. Now, motorboats can reach Jiading directly. Looking at the towering mountains on both sides of the Min River from the motorboat, you will feel like you have already entered the mountains and are already climbing. The water of the Min River is as swift as the streams in the valleys, and the color of the water is as clear as the water in the caves. The forests on both banks hang directly from the mountain ridges and cliffs to the riverbank. Before noon, the sunlight will not shine on the motorboat sailing on the river. It is like entering the Shanyin road, with strange grasses and trees on both sides, the songs of birds, the cries of monkeys, and the whistling of pines along the eaves, accompanying the small boat.

Disembark and head straight to Emei County. You can take a car, a sedan chair, or a rickshaw. But it is best to take a rickshaw, because the scenery along the way can only be fully appreciated if you travel slowly. Before reaching Mount Emei, you will pass many smaller Mount Emeis that are just as beautiful. We do not know why the mountains in western Sichuan are so beautiful. They are naturally dangerous, but they do not appear crude or terrifying at all, and they have the curves of a young maiden. The trees on the mountains are naturally lush and dense, but they are always arranged sparsely and evenly, with no crowded or isolated spots, and no bare mountains. The best thing is the water in the mountains: streams, ponds, and waterfalls. You can hear the sound of water at any time by the stone steps and in the forests. The leaves and petals of every mountain peak can flow into the great river below.

Mount Emei is a sacred place, as famous as Mount Wutai in Shanxi and Putuo in Zhejiang. The construction of roads and temples throughout Mount Emei, if not for the power of the Bodhisattvas, could not have achieved such results as they have now, right? There are no fewer than one hundred and several dozen temples on the entire mountain, and the roads built up and down, just the main roads alone, are more than one hundred li long. But is it the spirit of the gods or the power of the people? For example, every year, no fewer than tens of thousands of people from all over the country go to "pay pilgrimage to Mount Emei." Especially in the hot summer, travelers go to escape the heat, and pilgrims go to celebrate the "Ghost Festival in July." Therefore, there is an endless stream of travelers along the way. People who "burn incense" have a yellow cloth "pocket" tied around their waists, a large "bundle" on their backs, and some hold "walking sticks" while others knock on wooden fish. Moreover, among the pilgrims, there are more women than men, and more elderly people than young people. The 120-li-high Mount Emei takes them several or ten days to travel back and forth. The temples on the mountain rely entirely on the "merit money" and "incense money" donated by the pilgrims to maintain themselves. In addition, they can earn some money by providing food and lodging for guests. Mount Emei does not produce much grain, and almost all the thousands of monks on the mountain depend on the guests for a living.

Once you arrive at Baoguo Temple, the climb begins. At the foot of the mountain, the mountain path is still very flat and wide. Looking up, you can only see the cloud-covered peaks, and only faintly see the mountain peaks peeking out from the gaps in the clouds. Except for the mountain paths, forests, temples, and pedestrians within the nearest few li, which you can vaguely distinguish, the surrounding and upper mountain peaks are all buried in the sea of clouds. The mountain road is winding, because the higher you go, the steeper the mountain becomes, so the path has to meander and spiral upwards. People traveling together in front sometimes cannot see those behind, and those behind cannot see those in front. Many temples are hidden in the dense forests, and you will only discover them when you reach them. It truly fits the saying, "Just when you think the mountains and rivers have ended and there is no road, willows darken and flowers brighten to reveal another village." A huge Buddhist hall stands quietly and solemnly in the mountain valley and forest. Inside, all is silent, and only the sound of the wooden fish can be heard. This sound, with its rhythm, echoes back from the opposite mountain.

The steeper the mountain, the higher you go. Once you reach Snake's Retreat and Ninety-Nine Turns, it is probably the steepest it can get, right? What is called "Snake's Retreat"? It means that even snakes cannot climb up from here; even if they do, they will slide back down. Ninety-Nine Turns means that the mountain road twists and turns ninety-nine times within four or five li. People who cannot walk uphill hire "porters." The "porters" carry a "back frame" on their backs, placing the guests on their backs and climbing up the mountain. Because the mountain is so steep, they cannot use "sedan chairs" carried by two people, but can only use "back frames" carried by one person. The scenery behind Mount Emei and below the mountain, you cannot look up at the scenery above and to the left and right. Because if you are not careful, you will fall from the ten-thousand-zhang cliff. But when you reach the stone steps that are slightly wider, you will go into the deep valley. Looking at the deep ravines and cliffs below, your head will spin and your eyes will blur. However, the porter does not care; he can move and turn the back frame at will. At this time, your life is completely entrusted to the porter.

Once you reach Elephant Washing Pool and Nine Elders Cave, you have gone halfway up Mount Emei, and it has probably taken a day and a half or two days. There are many caves and pools on Mount Emei, but the most famous cave is Nine Elders Cave, and the most famous pool is Elephant Washing Pool. Nine Elders Cave is nine li deep. We only actually explored three li of it, and the path inside became very narrow, requiring torches to walk. Along the way, there are clear pools of water. It is said that this cave can lead directly to the back of the mountain, but no one has ever walked through it, for fear of encountering pythons inside. Above Nine Elders Cave and below Elephant Washing Pool, there are many monkeys along the way, coming out of the forests in groups, begging for food such as bread from passing guests. They are not afraid at all, and sometimes even steal the clothes of lone travelers. After passing Elephant Washing Pool, the climate is completely different from that down the mountain. If you go to Mount Emei in the hot summer, you can experience the four seasons of spring, summer, autumn, and winter. At the foot of the mountain, it is summer; at the waist of the mountain, it is spring and autumn; and at the top of the mountain, it is winter. Even in the height of summer, you must prepare cotton-padded clothing to go up the mountain.

After passing Prince Terrace and Founder Hall, you will reach the Golden Summit. Once you reach the Golden Summit, it is only four or five li from the summit, and you can overlook the entire mountain from here. Looking straight down from the summit, you can see that the many mountain peaks below are like lotus petals, heavily surrounding the main peak, like stars surrounding the North Star. Half of the mountain below is buried in clouds and mist. There are many ridges, near and far, appearing and disappearing from time to time, like islands in the sea or fishing boats drifting on the sea. White clouds form piles, one after another, like white cotton. Down the mountain, the sound of thunder comes from the sky, but at the summit, you only hear the rumbling thunder rising from under your feet. From the Golden Summit, walk dozens of steps to the Cloud Viewing Platform. In the afternoon, when the sun is setting, if you stand on the Cloud Viewing Platform and look out, you can see various wonderful Buddhist temples and statues appearing in the sky above Mount Emei, shining with golden light and dazzling the eyes. Behind the Cloud Viewing Platform is the Body Offering Cliff. Climbing up and standing on the cliff, you can see a ten-thousand-zhang-deep ravine with no bottom in sight, causing the mind to tremble. It is said that if you jump down from here, you can instantly become a Buddha, so it is called the Body Offering Cliff. The air at the summit is thin, and there is often cloud and rain. The entire day is filled with mist, with no clear sunny days. When there are many tourists, if everyone shouts loudly or beats the pilgrimage gongs and drums, fine drizzle will immediately fall from the sky. This is due to the thin air and very low air pressure. Therefore, water will not boil when heated at the summit.

From the Golden Summit to the Thousand Buddha Summit, and from the Thousand Buddha Summit to the Ten Thousand Buddha Summit, you have reached the absolute peak of Mount Emei. Once you reach the Ten Thousand Buddha Summit, you will feel that this peak is too lonely, because most of the peaks below are hidden and do not appear, or if they do appear, they are far away, low, and insignificant, unable to stand alongside it. As for the other mountains outside Mount Emei, no matter whether you use your naked eyes or a telescope, you cannot see them. However, on a slightly clearer day, you can see very far, even to the foot of the mountain, the town of Emei at the bottom of the mountain, the Min River dozens of li away, and even many villages. It is best to do it at night. Even at night, the summit is not very dark, perhaps because it is closer to the starlight. In this half of the sky, there is silence and vastness, as if detached from the human world. Below the mountain, there are countless bright lights, scattered like the stars in the sky. Especially at Puxian Temple, you can see even more. As the saying goes, "Ten thousand bright lamps pay homage to Puxian." During the day, you cannot see anything below the mountain; the clouds and mist separate everything below from above. At night... (continues on page 5)
